        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.4c06830"><meta property="og:title" content="Achieving High-Performance Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/acsami.4c06830.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) is emerging as a popular cathode for sodium-ion batteries owing to its stable structure, high operating voltage, and large energy density. However, its practical application is hindered by its low conductivity. In addition, due to the loss of fluorine during synthesis, Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) impurity is often easily generated, resulting in a decrease in actual operating voltage. Herein, a bifunctional carbon network composed of an N-doped carbon layer and carbon bridge is constructed around NVPF particles. Through pyrolysis of polydopamine (PDA), the NVPF particles are covered in situ by an N-doped carbon layer, and the carbon bridge generated by polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) is also coated with N-doped carbon. Besides, PTFE also serves as a fluorine supplement to ensure that pure NVPF is obtained. As a result, the bifunctional N-doped carbon network-modified NVPF delivers a high reversible capacity (125.7 mA h g–1 at 0.2 C) and appreciable cycle stability (92.7% at 1 C over 300 cycles, and 89.8% at 10 C over 1500 cycles). When assembled into a full cell with a commercial hard carbon anode, it displays a discharge median voltage of up to 3.62 V at 0.2 C. Furthermore, it achieves a high energy density of 373.7 W h kg–1 at a power density of 461.2 W kg–1, with an excellent specific energy retention of 78.2% after 200 cycles. Therefore, this modification method is expected to be extended to other fluorine-containing materials with poor electrical conductivity."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/acsami.4c06830.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da8b0faa65b325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8b0faa65b325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'a9c70c98-ba85-40dc-b4aa-831cbe04523c'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90da8b0faa65b325-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8b0faa65b325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

data-references="https://pubs.acs.org/action/ajaxShowEnhancedAbstract?doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06830&amp;ajax=true" data-enable-mathjax="true" vocab="http://schema.org/" typeof="ScholarlyArticle" href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c06830" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite Interfaces</i></span><span class="cit-fg-year"> 2024</span><span class="cit-fg-volume">, 16</span><span class="cit-fg-issue">, 27</span><span class="cit-fg-pageRange">, 35179-35189</span></span></span></div></div></div></div></div><input type="hidden" name="aamick" id="copyRights" value="/pb-assets/json/journal-info-1738791784303.json"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone5" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone5"><!-- Article Refresh Event Tracking -->
<script nonce="90da8b0faa65b325-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Achieving High-Performance Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;F&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c06830", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

        </div></div><div class="article__pubdate"><span>Energy, Environmental, and Catalysis Applications</span><time datetime="2024-06-25">June 25, 2024</time></div><h1 class="article_header-title" tabindex="0"><span class="hlFld-Title" property="headline">Achieving High-Performance Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Cathode Material through a Bifunctional N-Doped Carbon Network</span><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy article link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Article link copied!</span></div></h1><ul class="loa"><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">Chang Sun</span><div class="loa-info hlFld-Affiliation"><div class="loa-info--wrapper"><div class="loa-info-name">Chang Sun</div><div class="loa-info-affiliations"><div class="loa-info-affiliations-info">Hubei Provincial Collaborative Innovation Center for New Energy Microgrid, College of Electrical Engineering &amp; New Energy, China Three Gorges University, Yichang 443002, P. href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D35179%26pageCount%3D11%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DChang%2BSun%252C%2BLu-Lu%2BZhang%252C%2BZe-Rong%2BDeng%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D27%26contentID%3Dacsami.4c06830%26title%3DAchieving%2BHigh-Performance%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bthrough%2Ba%2BBifunctional%2BN-Doped%2BCarbon%2BNetwork%26numPages%3D11%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D35189%26publicationDate%3DJuly%2B2024" data-id="article_rights_permissions">Request reuse permissions</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> (NVPF) is emerging as a popular cathode for sodium-ion batteries owing to its stable structure, high operating voltage, and large energy density. However, its practical application is hindered by its low conductivity. In addition, due to the loss of fluorine during synthesis, Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) impurity is often easily generated, resulting in a decrease in actual operating voltage. Herein, a bifunctional carbon network composed of an N-doped carbon layer and carbon bridge is constructed around NVPF particles. Through pyrolysis of polydopamine (PDA), the NVPF particles are covered in situ by an N-doped carbon layer, and the carbon bridge generated by polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) is also coated with N-doped carbon. Besides, PTFE also serves as a fluorine supplement to ensure that pure NVPF is obtained. As a result, the bifunctional N-doped carbon network-modified NVPF delivers a high reversible capacity (125.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2 C) and appreciable cycle stability (92.7% at 1 C over 300 cycles, and 89.8% at 10 C over 1500 cycles). When assembled into a full cell with a commercial hard carbon anode, it displays a discharge median voltage of up to 3.62 V at 0.2 C. Furthermore, it achieves a high energy density of 373.7 W h kg<sup>–1</sup> at a power density of 461.2 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, with an excellent specific energy retention of 78.2% after 200 cycles. Therefore, this modification method is expected to be extended to other fluorine-containing materials with poor electrical conductivity.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D35179%26pageCount%3D11%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DChang%2BSun%252C%2BLu-Lu%2BZhang%252C%2BZe-Rong%2BDeng%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D27%26contentID%3Dacsami.4c06830%26title%3DAchieving%2BHigh-Performance%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bthrough%2Ba%2BBifunctional%2BN-Doped%2BCarbon%2BNetwork%26numPages%3D11%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D35189%26publicationDate%3DJuly%2B2024" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2024 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291337&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Carbon" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Carbon" class="article__tags__link">Carbon</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291952&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrochemical cells" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrochemical%20cells" class="article__tags__link">Electrochemical cells</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291637&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Energy density" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Energy%20density" class="article__tags__link">Energy density</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292395&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Fluorine" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Fluorine" class="article__tags__link">Fluorine</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Cathode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_cathode">cathode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Na3v22f3&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Na3V2%28PO4%292F3">Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Bifunctional+Carbon+Network&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_bifunctional%20carbon%20network">bifunctional carbon network</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=N-doping&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_N-doping">N-doping</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">In recent years, due to the limited and uneven distribution of lithium resources, the price of lithium salts fluctuates greatly, which has brought adverse effects on the development of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> As a complementary technology to LIBs, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are increasingly valued due to their rich raw materials, good safety, excellent low-temperature performance, and fast charging characteristics. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3 ref4 ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 3 to 5">(3−5)</a> Cathode material is a critical component that affects the working voltage and energy density of SIBs. Significant efforts have been made in the modification of cathode materials for SIBs, including transition-metal oxides, polyanionic compounds, Prussian blue analogs, and organic compounds. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15" aria-label="reference 6 to 15">(6−15)</a> Among them, NASICON-type Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> (NVPF), as a typical polyanionic compound, is a promising cathode material for SIBs owing to its high working voltage (∼3.8 V) and large theoretical capacity (∼128 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16 ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 16 and 17">(16,17)</a> NVPF has an open three-dimensional (3D) frame structure composed of [PO<sub>4</sub>] tetrahedron and [V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>8</sub>F<sub>3</sub>] double-octahedron, which is conducive to Na ions diffusion. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> Nevertheless, its low electronic conductivity always leads to inferior capacity, which greatly hinders its utilization. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19" aria-label="reference 19">(19)</a> To address this issue, various methods, including coating, doping, and structure design, have been employed to modify NVPF. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 20 to 23">(20−23)</a> Among them, carbon coating is more favored due to its abundant carbon sources and excellent electronic conductivity. In addition, the carbon coating layer can also serve as a buffer medium to reduce the volume change of NVPF caused by Na-ion extraction/insertion, and as a barrier to suppress side reactions between NVPF and electrolyte, which are beneficial for maintaining the cycling stability of NVPF. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24 ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref25" aria-label="reference 24 and 25">(24,25)</a> Especially, doping carbon layer with heteroatoms not only can enhance the electronic conductivity but also promote ion migration and storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> Dopamine (DA), as an N-containing carbon source, has excellent adhesion due to the existence of 5,6-dihydroxyindole group, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> so it can form a uniform and complete polydopamine (PDA) nanocoating layer on the surface of many materials. When calcined at high temperatures, the obtained PDA is further pyrolyzed into a continuous N-doped carbon coating layer, which is conducive to promoting electrolyte infiltration, improving electronic conductivity, and enhancing Na ions migration. In addition to the poor electronic conductivity of NVPF, during the high-temperature calcination process of NVPF synthesis due to the loss of fluorine, NVP impurity is often prone to occur. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29" aria-label="reference 28 and 29">(28,29)</a> Polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) contains not only carbon but also fluorine, which has been successfully used as not only a carbon source but also as a fluorine source to reduce or even eliminate NVP impurity.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, we used PTFE as a supplementary fluorine and carbon source, as well as DA as an N-containing carbon source, to construct a bifunctional carbon network composed of an N-doped carbon layer and a carbon bridge around NVPF particles. On the one hand, PTFE can compensate for the loss of fluorine during high-temperature calcination, suppress the generation of NVP impurity, achieve the expected working voltage, and thus obtain satisfactory energy density. On the other hand, DA can act as a nitrogen source to dope the carbon coating layer around NVPF particles and carbon bridges, resulting in defects in the carbon layer and providing additional sodium storage sites. Moreover, the bifunctional N-doped carbon network not only can improve the electron/ion transfer environment at the electrode material interface but also prevents NVPF from being corroded by electrolytes and stabilizes the material structure. Owing to the bifunctional N-doped carbon network, NVPF displays higher capacity and superior cycle performance in both half cells and full cells, showing great potential for application in high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The NC/C@NVPF and comparative material (NC@NVPF) were prepared by the sol–gel method followed by heat treatment, as displayed in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sch1" aria-label="Scheme 1">Scheme 1</a>. First, citric acid and V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> were dissolved in deionized water under magnetic stirring at 60 °C for 30 min. Later, stoichiometric amounts of NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> and NaF were also dissolved in the above solution to obtain a uniform sol. When the solvent was thoroughly volatilized, a blue-green gel was obtained. After being ground, the gel powders were dried in a vacuum oven at 80 °C overnight and then preheated to 300 °C under N<sub>2</sub> for 4 h to form a precursor. Subsequently, the precursor and PTFE dispersion (5 wt % of precursor) were homogeneously mixed in ethanol for 6 h, with a concentration of 60 wt % PTFE dispersion. After filtrating, drying, and grinding, the acquired mixture was heated to 600 °C under N<sub>2</sub> for 8 h to obtain NVPF. And then, the NVPF powders were evenly dispersed in a Tris solution (pH ≈ 8.5) with DA (10 wt % of NVPF) and PTFE dispersion (40 wt % of NVPF) and stirred for 24 h. After filtrating, drying, and grinding, the mixture was heated to 600 °C under N<sub>2</sub> for 8 h to obtain a bifunctional N-doped carbon network-modified NVPF sample (denoted as NC/C@NVPF). As a control, the N-doped C-coated NVPF sample was also prepared using the same process (denoted as NC@NVPF). Here, only 5 wt % of PTFE dispersion was added to supplement the fluorine loss during the synthesis process.</div><figure id="sch1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Scheme 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0007.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><div class="title2">Scheme 1. Schematic Diagram of the Preparation Route of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF</div></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=sch1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">Before preparing NC/C@NVPF, we explored the dosage of PTFE as a fluorine supplement agent and optimized the dosage of DA. As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>, the electrochemical performance of three samples (such as NVPF without modification, NVPF modified by 3 and 5 wt % PTFE, denoted as b-NVPF, 3% PTFE@NVPF, and 5% PTFE@NVPF, respectively) was compared. As the dosage of PTFE increases, the voltage plateau corresponding to NVP impurity becomes more and more obscure at approximately 3.4/3.3 V. When NVPF was modified with 5 wt % PTFE, the plateau corresponding to NVP disappears and, thus, 5 wt % PTFE can be used as the minimum dose for fluorine supplementation. Besides, it is also found that the electrochemical performance of 10 wt % DA-modified NVPF (denoted as 10% NC@NVPF) is the best (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2a and b</a>), with a discharge specific capacity of 106.4 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> and a capacity retention rate of 95.0% after 150 cycles at 1 C, as listed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>. Therefore, we chose the NVPF sample comodified with 5 wt % PTFE and 10 wt % DA as the control group (denoted as NC@NVPF). Furthermore, to exclude the possibility that the electrochemical performance of NC/C@NVPF is optimal due to its high carbon content, we prepared an NVPF sample modified with 18 wt % DA but without PTFE (denoted as NC@NVPF-N<sub>PTFE</sub>), with a carbon content of 5.18 wt %, close to NC/C@NVPF. As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2c,d</a>, NC@NVPF-N<sub>PTFE</sub> exhibits three pairs of obvious platforms during the charge/discharge process. Among them, the platforms located at 3.7/3.6 V and 4.2/4.1 V belong to NVPF, while the platform at 3.4/3.3 V is related to NVP impurity generated during high-temperature calcination process at 600 °C due to fluorine loss. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> NC@NVPF-N<sub>PTFE</sub> has a similar carbon content, but its reversible capacity at 1 C is only 87.4 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, which is lower than NC/C@NVPF (107.4 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>).</div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i5">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">XRD patterns of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF are displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a. All diffraction peaks are consistent with the standard tetragonal NVPF phase (PDF#04-012-2207) with the <i>P</i>4<sub>2</sub>/<i>mnm</i> space group, indicating that the introduction of DA and PTFE as carbon sources does not affect the crystal structure of NVPF. The two samples exhibit high crystallinity and no impurities. To provide more detailed information on the lattice structure of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF, Rietveld refinements are performed based on XRD data (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b,c). As listed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a>, the refined lattice parameters for NC@NVPF are <i>a</i> = <i>b</i> = 9.0493 Å, <i>c</i> = 10.7271 Å, and <i>V</i> = 878.45 Å<sup>3</sup> (<i>R</i><sub>wp</sub> = 7.01%, <i>R</i><sub>p</sub> = 5.27%), and for NC/C@NVPF, the lattice parameters are <i>a</i> = <i>b</i> = 9.0434 Å, <i>c</i> = 10.7280 Å, and <i>V</i> = 877.37 Å<sup>3</sup> (<i>R</i><sub>wp</sub> = 6.30%, <i>R</i><sub>p</sub> = 4.96%). <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>d shows the crystal structure of NC/C@NVPF, which possesses a 3D framework composed of a [V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>8</sub>F<sub>3</sub>] double octahedron and a [PO<sub>4</sub>] tetrahedron. Na ions occupy the interstitial positions between the [VO<sub>4</sub>F<sub>2</sub>] octahedral units, which is conducive to their own deintercalation and intercalation during the charging and discharging processes. Besides, no diffraction peaks related to carbon were detected in the two samples, indicating that carbon formed during the pyrolysis of PDA and PTFE is amorphous. To further investigate the structure of carbon in the two samples, Raman spectra were analyzed in detail. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>e, the characteristic D and G peaks corresponding to disordered carbon and graphitic carbon can be observed at ∼1350 and ∼1580 cm<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. The area ratio of the D peak to the G peak (<i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub>) can be used as an indicator to evaluate the degree of disorder or graphitization of carbon. By calculation, the <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> values of both samples are greater than 1, indicating a considerable degree of disorder in the carbon of both samples. Moreover, the <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> value of NC/C@NVPF (1.32) is higher than NC@NVPF (1.23), demonstrating a higher disorder degree in the carbon of NC/C@NVPF. The higher degree of disorder means more defects in residual carbon of NC/C@NVPF, which is conducive to promoting charge transfer and providing more sodium storage sites. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31 ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31,32)</a> Furthermore, as listed in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table 1</a>, the carbon contents of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF were determined to be 3.76 and 5.27 wt %, and the electronic conductivity of two samples was measured to be 1.81 × 10<sup>–4</sup> and 2.06 × 10<sup>–4</sup> S cm<sup>–1</sup>, respectively.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0001.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a) X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns and (b,c) Rietveld refined XRD patterns of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF, (d) crystal structure of NC/C@NVPF, (e) Raman spectra, (f) X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) full spectra of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF, (g–i) V 2p, C 1s, and N 1s high-resolution XPS spectra of NC/C@NVPF, respectively, and (j–l) V 2p, C 1s, and N 1s high-resolution XPS spectra of NC@NVPF, respectively.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Carbon Content and Electronic Conductivity of the Two Samples</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="table "><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="×"></colgroup><thead><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">sample</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">carbon content (wt&nbsp;%)</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char="×">electronic conductivity (S&nbsp;cm–<sup>1</sup>)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NC@NVPF</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">3.76</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char="×">1.81&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>–4</sup></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NC/C@NVPF</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">5.27</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char="×">2.06&nbsp;×10<sup>–4</sup></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">XPS was utilized to investigate the surface chemical composition of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF. From the full spectra (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>f), it can be seen that in addition to Na, V, P, O, and F, both samples also contain C and N. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>g–i displays the high-resolution V 2p, C 1s, and N 1s spectra of both samples. As exhibited in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>g,j, two intensive peaks at about 523.8 and 517.3 eV belong to V 2p<sub>1/2</sub> and V 2p<sub>3/2</sub>, respectively, confirming the existence of trivalent V in both NC/C@NVPF and NC@NVPF. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> The high-resolution C 1s spectra of NC/C@NVPF and NC@NVPF (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>h,k) can be fitted to four peaks located at about 284.7, 285.3, 286.2, and 288.5 eV, corresponding to C═C, C–C, C–N, and O–C═O/C–F bonds, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 34 and 35">(34,35)</a> Combined with the C–F (688.5 eV) bond displayed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> it can be proved that the carbon generated from the pyrolysis of DA and PTFE was successfully coated on the surface of NVPF. In addition, compared with NC@NVPF (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3a</a>), NC/C@NVPF exhibits a relatively stronger C–F peak (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3b</a>), due to its higher carbon content generated by the carbonization of more PTFE. And the peaks related to V–F bond (684.5 eV) of both samples demonstrate the successful substitution of PO<sub>4</sub><sup>3–</sup> group by F<sup>–</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> Also, the N 1s spectra of NC/C@NVPF and NC@NVPF (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>i,l) can be fitted to four characteristic peaks, namely, pyridinic N (398.5 eV), pyrrolic N (399.5 eV), graphitic N (401.0 eV), and oxidized N (404.1 eV). Wherein, both pyridinic and pyrrolic N related to defects can promote Na<sup>+</sup> migration and provide additional sodium storage sites. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37 ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 37 and 38">(37,38)</a> Notably, the proportion of pyridinic N and pyrrolic N in NC@NVPF is 39.72%, while their proportion in NC/C@NVPF is 44.54%. The larger amounts of pyridinic N and pyrrolic N in NC/C@NVPF reveal more defects in its carbon network, which is more conducive to promoting Na<sup>+</sup> migration and providing more sodium storage sites.</div><div class="NLM_p">The micromorphology and structure of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF were investigated by TEM. It can be clearly observed from <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a,c that the two samples present irregular particle morphology and NVPF particles are connected by some carbon bridges. The lattice fringes with spacings of 0.553 and 0.331 nm in NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b,d) correspond to the (111) and (103) crystal planes of NVPF, respectively, indicating their excellent crystallinity. Also, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b,d clearly shows that the NVPF particles are evenly wrapped by amorphous carbon with nano thickness. In addition, the EDS mappings presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e not only prove that Na, V, P, O, F, C, and N elements are uniformly distributed in NC/C@NVPF, but also verify the existence of carbon bridges composed of N-doped C.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0002.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a,b) Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images of NC@NVPF, (c,d) TEM images of NC/C@NVPF, and (e) HAADF image and corresponding EDS mappings of NC/C@NVPF.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Cyclic voltammetry (CV) and galvanostatic charge/discharge tests were conducted to examine the electrochemical performance of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a displays the CV curves of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF in the first cycle. Both samples exhibit two pairs of distinct redox peaks, located at 3.7/3.6 and 4.2/4.1 V, respectively. Wherein, the redox peaks at around 3.7/3.6 V are related to the extraction/reinsertion process of first Na<sup>+</sup> from/into the Na2 sites, and the redox peaks at around 4.2/4.1 V are assigned to the extraction/reinsertion process of second Na<sup>+</sup> from/into Na1 sites. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref33 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref33 ref39" aria-label="reference 28, 33 and 39">(28,33,39)</a> As listed in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl2" href="#tbl2">Table 2</a>, NC/C@NVPF presents the smaller voltage difference between oxidation peaks and reduction peaks than NC@NVPF, which illustrates the weaker polarization and the better reversibility of NC/C@NVPF. In addition, the CV curves of two samples in the first three cycles are also shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>, and the high overlapping of the CV curves of both samples reveals the stable process of sodiation and desodiation. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b,c exhibits the first charge/discharge curves and cycle performance of two samples at 0.2 C. Both samples display two pairs of voltage platforms at 3.7/3.6 and 4.2/4.1 V in the charge/discharge process, which is consistent with the CV curves. Especially, NC/C@NVPF delivers a higher initial discharge capacity of 125.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with an outstanding capacity retention rate of 93.5% after 100 cycles, which is superior to NC@NVPF (117.3 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, 78.6%). At 1 C, as displayed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d, the capacity of NC/C@NVPF reaches a relatively steady state after 10 cycles, and the corresponding discharge specific capacity is 114.3 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at the 10th cycle, which is larger than that of NC@NVPF (106.1 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>). After 300 cycles, as presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>e, NC/C@NVPF still delivers a higher capacity of 106.0 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with a more appreciable capacity retention rate of 92.7% than NC@NVPF (77.1 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, 72.7%). To evaluate the current tolerance of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF, the two samples were cycled from 0.2 to 10 C and then returned to 0.2 C. As presented in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S3</a>, NC/C@NVPF exhibits higher average reversible capacities at different current rates of 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 C, with values of 124.9, 122.9, 119.4, 114.3, 100.2, and 87.1 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. When the current rate returns to 0.2 C after 60 cycles, its average reversible capacity recovers to 122.6 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, with a capacity recovery rate of up to 98.1%, which is better than that of NC@NVPF (96.8%). This result reflects the excellent current tolerance of NC/C@NVPF. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> Furthermore, the long-term cycle performance, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>g, confirms that NC/C@NVPF has a more stable average capacity of 87.2 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with a capacity retention of 89.8% after 1500 cycles at 10 C, which is better than that of NC@NVPF (60.9 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, 72.4%). Even compared with the recently reported NVPF cathodes, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref39 ref40 ref41 ref42 ref43 ref44 ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref39 ref40 ref41 ref42 ref43 ref44 ref45" aria-label="reference 23 and 39 to 45">(23,39−45)</a> as listed in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl3" href="#tbl3">Table 3</a>, NC/C@NVPF still delivers superior electrochemical performance, including capacity, rate, and cycling. The satisfactory electrochemistry performance can be attributed to the bifunctional N-doped carbon network formed by the pyrolysis of DA and PTFE. On the one hand, the carbon coating layer serves as a protective layer, which can better restrain the side reactions between NVPF and the electrolyte. Also, it can serve as a buffer medium to reduce the volume change of NVPF caused by Na<sup>+</sup> extraction/insertion, thereby stabilizing its structure. On the other hand, the carbon bridge is beneficial for improving the electronic conductivity of NVPF and the Na<sup>+</sup> transfer efficiency between NVPF and electrolyte.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0003.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Electrochemical performance of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF: (a) CV curves of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF for the first cycle at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> in the range 2.0–4.5 V, (b,c) the first charge/discharge curves and cycle performance of two samples at 0.2 C, respectively, (d) cycle performance at 1 C, (e) the 10th and 300th charge/discharge curves at 1 C, (f) rate performance, and (g) long-term cycle performance at 10 C.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl2"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 2. Voltage Difference between Oxidation and Reduction Peaks of Two Samples in CV Curves</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="table "><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="."></colgroup><thead><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">&nbsp;</th><th class="rowsep1 colsep0" colspan="2" scope="col" align="center" char=".">voltage difference (V)</th></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">sample</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">O1-R1</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">O2-R2</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NC@NVPF</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.22</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.10</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NC/C@NVPF</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.19</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.08</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl3"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 3. Comparison of Electrochemical Performance between NC/C@NVPF and the Other NVPF Cathodes</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="table "><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="left"><col align="left"><col align="left"><col align="left"></colgroup><thead><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">samples</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">discharge capacity</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">rate performance</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">capacity retention</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">ref</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NC/C@NVPF</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">124.9&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;0.2&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">87.1&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;10&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">89.8%/10&nbsp;C/1500&nbsp;cycles</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">this work</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">c-NVPF@NC</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">121.7&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;0.2&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">54.7&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;20&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">77.6%/10&nbsp;C/1000&nbsp;cycles</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23');
