return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">(42)</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NVPF-3.4&nbsp;wt&nbsp;%C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">116.4&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;0.2&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">60.7&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;20&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">82.1%/10&nbsp;C/1200&nbsp;cycles</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">(43)</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NVPF@NC</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">120.3&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;0.1&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">85.0&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;10&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">72.7%/5&nbsp;C/500&nbsp;cycles</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" aria-label="reference 44">(44)</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">NVPF@C-T</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">124.5&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;0.2&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">98.8&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g–<sup>1</sup>&nbsp;at&nbsp;10&nbsp;C</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">94.8%/10&nbsp;C/300&nbsp;cycles</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">To demonstrate the effect of a bifunctional N-doped carbon network on the electrochemical performance, the kinetic properties of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF were surveyed by electrochemical impedance spectroscopy and the GITT. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a, the Nyquist plots of two samples exhibit a small intercept, an obvious semicircle, and a sloping line. Among them, the semicircle in the middle-high frequency range on behalf of the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref46" aria-label="reference 46">(46)</a> The Nyquist plots were fitted with the “R[C(RW)]” equivalent circuit (the inset in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>a) to acquire the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value of two samples. By comparison, the NC/C@NVPF electrode exhibits a smaller <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value (328.8 Ω) than NC@NVPF (476.2 Ω), indicating a better charge transfer environment in NC/C@NVPF with a bifunctional N-doped carbon network. In addition, <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b displays the slope of the relationship lines between Z′ and ω<sup>–1/2</sup> of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF. According to <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">eq S1</a>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47 ref48'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 47 and 48">(47,48)</a> the lower slope (σ) reveals the faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics of NC/C@NVPF. Both the lower <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and faster Na ions diffusion kinetics confirm that the bifunctional N-doped carbon network facilitates electrons and ions transfer. The GITT curves of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF at different voltages are listed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c. The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub>) value can be calculated according to <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">eq S2</a>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49 ref50'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49 ref50" aria-label="reference 49 and 50">(49,50)</a> As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>d, Δ<i>E</i><sub>S</sub>, Δ<i>E</i><sub>τ</sub>, and τ in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">eq S2</a> can be calculated from the GITT curves. From <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>e, it can be seen that both samples exhibit two minimum values of <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> during the charging and discharging processes. The minimum values of <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> are located around 3.7/3.6 and 4.2/4.1 V, which are coincident with the location of the redox peaks in the CV curves and voltage platforms in the charging/discharging profiles. The minimum values of <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> usually correspond to the phase transition process of electrode material. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> Regardless of whether Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> is converted to Na<sub>2</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>, or Na<sub>2</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> is converted to NaV<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>, NC/C@NVPF has a higher sodium ion diffusion coefficient than NC@NVPF. Even at the beginning of Na<sup>+</sup> extraction, NC/C@NVPF also has a faster sodium ion diffusion kinetics than NC@NVPF. During the charging process, the average Na ion diffusion coefficients of NC/C@NVPF and NC@NVPF are 1.43 × 10<sup>–11</sup> and 1.03 × 10<sup>–11</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. During the discharging process, the average Na ion diffusion coefficients of NC/C@NVPF and NC@NVPF are 1.70 × 10<sup>–11</sup> and 1.36 × 10<sup>–11</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. Obviously, whether during the charging or discharging process, the <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> values of NC/C@NVPF are higher than those of NC@NVPF. This result further confirms that the bifunctional N-doped carbon network has a positive effect on the diffusion kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup>.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0004.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Electrochemical kinetic performance of samples: (a) Nyquist plots and corresponding equivalent circuit diagram of samples, (b) relationship lines between Z′ and ω<sup>–1/2</sup> in the low-frequency region, (c) galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) curves, (d) single GITT step of NC/C@NVPF during the discharge process, and (e) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients during charge and discharge process.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To investigate the V dissolution of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF after different cycles, the separator states before and after 50, 100, 200, and 300 cycles are compared in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>a. As the number of cycles increases, the color of separators corresponding to NC@NVPF significantly darkens, while the color of separators related to NC/C@NVPF does not present an obvious change. This may be attributed to the lower V dissolution amount of NC/C@NVPF in the electrolyte during the cycling process compared to NCVPF. To further demonstrate this conclusion, NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF electrode sheets were soaked in 1 mL of 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> electrolyte for 20 days, and then the ICP–MS tests were conducted on the electrolyte. The content of V in the electrolyte after soaking the NC@NVPF electrode sheet is 0.326 μg g<sup>–1</sup>, while the content of V in the electrolyte after soaking the NC/C@NVPF electrode sheet is only 0.098 μg g<sup>–1</sup>. This implies that the bifunctional N-doped carbon network can more effectively inhibit the dissolution of V.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0005.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) Optical photos of the separators after different cycles and (b,c) Rietveld refined XRD patterns of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF after 300 cycles, respectively.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In addition, the cell volumes of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF before and after 300 cycles were also compared to explore the positive effect of bifunctional N-doped carbon network on stabilizing crystal structure. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 5</a>b,c exhibits the Rietveld refined XRD patterns of two samples after 300 cycles; all diffraction peaks match well with the standard NVPF phase, and the values of <i>R</i><sub>wp</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>p</sub> are both less than 10%. As listed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a>, the cell volume of NC/C@NVPF before the cycle is 877.37 Å<sup>3</sup>, and after 300 cycles, its cell volume decreased to 876.89 Å<sup>3</sup>. The volume change rate is 0.05%, lower than NC@NVPF (0.61%). This result indicates that the bifunctional N-doped carbon network is beneficial for reducing the volume change caused by Na<sup>+</sup> extraction/insertion from/into NVPF during cycling.</div><div class="NLM_p">Using NC/C@NVPF as the cathode and CHC as the anode to assemble the full cells, we studied the practical application of NC/C@NVPF was studied. As displayed in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/suppl_file/am4c06830_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>, the CHC anode achieves a relatively stable capacity after ten cycles. Therefore, before assembling the full cell, all CHC anodes were first subjected to 10 cycles for electrochemical presodification and then reassembled with an NVPF cathode to acquire the full cells. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a shows the first charge/discharge curve of the NC/C@NVPF cathode, NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell, and the 10th charge/discharge curve of the CHC anode at the current density of 128 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. The NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell exhibits two clear charge and discharge platforms, with a discharge median voltage of up to 3.61 V, which means it has the potential to achieve high energy density. The operating principle diagram of the full cell is shown in the inset of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a. During the charging process, Na ions are extracted from the NVPF cathode and inserted into the CHC anode through an electrolyte and separator, while the discharge process is exactly the opposite. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>b presents the cycle stability of the NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell at 0.2 C. The full cell still has a capacity of 105.6 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> (based on the mass of NC/C@NVPF) after 50 cycles with 92.3% capacity retention. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>c displays the rate performance of NC/C@NVPF||CHC. The full cell delivers an average discharge specific capacity of 117.3, 113.6, 108.6, 103.8, 97.0, 90.3, 83.8, and 77.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at different rates of 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5 C, respectively. When the rate returns to 0.1 C, the full cell still maintains an average discharge specific capacity of 114.4 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, close to the initial discharge capacity of 117.3 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>, demonstrating its superior reversibility. When NC/C@NVPF||CHC was charged/discharged at 0.2 C for three cycles and then charged/discharged at 1 C (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>d), the full cell still exhibits a discharge capacity of 87.2 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> with a capacity retention of 85.3% after 200 cycles, which displays an appreciable cycle performance. The LED lamps illuminated by the NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>e confirm the practicality of NC/C@NVPF as the cathode for SIBs. More importantly, the NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell presents a high energy density of 407.7 W h kg<sup>–1</sup> at a power density of 92.7 W kg<sup>–1</sup>. When the power density reaches 461.2 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, the NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell exhibits a high energy density of 373.7 W h kg<sup>–1</sup>, and it still retains 78.2% of the specific energy after 200 cycles.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/medium/am4c06830_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0006.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. (a) Charge and discharge curves of the NC/C@NVPF cathode, commercial hard carbon (CHC) anode, and NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell at a current density of 128 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, (b) cycle performance of NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell at 0.2 C, (c) rate performance of NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell, (d) discharge specific capacity and cycle performance of NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell at 1 C, (e) LED lamps lighted by the NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell, and (f) discharge specific energy and cycle performance of NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell at 1 C. The inset in a shows the operating principle of the NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06830/asset/images/large/am4c06830_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06830&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i9">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In conclusion, the bifunctional N-doped carbon network composed of an N-doped carbon layer and carbon bridge was successfully constructed on the NVPF particles’ surface using DA and PTFE as double carbon sources. PTFE not only serves as a carbon source but also as a fluorine supplement, which has a positive impact on the working voltage of NVPF. As a cathode for SIBs, the NC/C@NVPF electrode exhibits a high discharge specific capacity of 125.7 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2 C and an excellent capacity retention ratio of 92.7% at 1 C over 300 cycles. Especially, it retains 89.8% of the initial capacity after 1500 cycles at 10 C. When assembled into a full cell with a CHC anode, it presents a discharge median voltage of up to 3.62 V and also delivers a satisfactory reversible capacity (117.3 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 C, and 77.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 5 C) and superior cycle performance (85.3% at 1 C over 200 cycles). More notably, the NC/C@NVPF||CHC full cell still displays a high energy density of 373.7 W h kg<sup>–1</sup> at a high power density of 461.2 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, with an excellent specific energy retention of 78.2% after 200 cycles, demonstrating enormous practical application potential.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div         </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the intrinsic electronic cond. of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF), zirconium (Zr) was introduced into the NVPF/C compd. through a carbothermal redn. reaction with citric acid as the carbon source.  The effects of Zr4+ doping on the crystal structure and morphol. of the as-prepd. materials were analyzed.  Electrochem. and kinetic properties of the samples were investigated by galvanostatic charge-discharge, CV and EIS test.  It is confirmed that moderate Zr4+ doping can improve the electrochem. performance of NVPF.  Among all Na3V2-xZrx(PO4)2F3/C (x = 0, 0.01, 0.05, 0.1) samples, Na3V1·95Zr0·05(PO4)2F3/C shows the best rate and cycle performance.  It exhibits the highest specific capacity of 121.8 and 110.3 mAh/g at 0.2 and 10 C, resp., and maintains a capacity retention of approx. 83.6% after 1000 cycles at 5 C.  The kinetic properties results show that the excellent electrochem. performance of Na3V1·95Zr0·05(PO4)2F3/C can be attributed to the increase in electronic cond. and ion diffusion coeff.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGocuKGVZkqh1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsCLEY2pJ8ag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsF2itbjF&amp;md5=808628143b860ee11f9794c4ffee157e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.3c12772"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Puspitasari, D.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N/P-Dual-Doped Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)2O2F Microspheres as a High-Performance Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Liu, Jing; Wei, Cheng; Sun, Pan-Pan; Gao, Lin; Ding, Xiao-Kai; Liang, Gan; Yang, Xue-Lin; Huang, Yun-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3670-3680</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2O2F (NVPOF) is attracting great interest due to its large capacity and high working voltage.  However, poor electronic cond. limits the electrochem. performance of NVPOF.  Herein, we fabricate N/P-dual-doped carbon-coated NVPOF microspheres (labeled as NVPOF@P/N/C) via a hydrothermal process followed by heat treatment.  This microsphere-structured NVPOF@P/N/C composite has a relatively high tap d. of 1.22 g/cm3.  TEM and XPS results reveal that the dual-doped carbon layer is tightly coated on the NVPOF surface due to the bridging effect of P and has a good protective effect on NVPOF.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. confirm that a N/P-dual-doped carbon layer is advantageous to achieve higher electronic cond. and lower migration activation energy than those of the undoped and single N- or P-doped carbon layer.  As a cathode material for a sodium-ion battery (SIB), NVPOF@P/N/C exhibits high capacity (128 mAh/g at 0.5 C and 122 mAh/g at 2 C) and ultralong cycle performance (only 0.037% capacity fading rate per cycle in 500 cycles at 2 C).  We believe that the NVPOF@P/N/C composite is appealing for high-performance SIBs with large energy d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoV3ugCQ6EW17Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAvnXJdbHrPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXisVKktb%252FL&amp;md5=4d63803cf4d5a30b27fcdf44b786310f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1039/C8DT00062J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multi-Heteroatom Doped Carbon Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Derived from Ionic Liquids</span>. <i>Dalton Trans.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>47</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4259</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4266</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8DT00062J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D47%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D4259-4266%26journal%3DDalton%2BTrans.%26author%3DL.-L.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.-X.%2BZhou%26author%3DT.%2BLi%26author%3DD.%2BMa%26author%3DX.-L.%2BYang%26title%3DMulti-Heteroatom%2BDoped%2BCarbon%2BCoated%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2BDerived%2Bfrom%2BIonic%2BLiquids%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC8DT00062J&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06830&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC8DT00062J&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multi-heteroatom doped carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 derived from ionic liquids</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Zhou, Ying-Xian; Li, Tao; Ma, Di; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">47</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4259-4266</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">DTARAF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1477-9226</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multi-heteroatom (N, S and F) doped carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 (labeled as NVP/C-ILs) derived from an ionic liq. 1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium bis(trifluoromethylsulfonyl)imide ([EMIM]TF2N) has been successfully fabricated.  The as-prepd. Na3V2(PO4)3 particles are well dispersed and closely coated with a multi-heteroatom (N, S and F) doped carbon layer.  As a cathode for sodium-ion batteries, the NVP/C-ILs electrode exhibits high reversible specific capacity (117.5 mA h g-1 at 1C), superior rate performance (93.4 mA h g-1 at 10C) and excellent cycling stability (∼95% capacity retention ratio at 10C over 1000 cycles).  The impressive electrochem. performance of NVP/C-ILs can be attributed to effectively conductive networks for electrons and Na+ ions induced by a joint effect of N, S and F doping on carbon.  The use of multi-heteroatom doped carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 provides a facile and effective strategy for the fabrication of high performance electrode materials with low intrinsic elec. cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqO6HYzDTDauLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAvnXJdbHrPQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced electrochemical performance of carbon and aluminum oxide co-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Di; Zhang, Lu-Lu; Li, Tao; Liu, Chang; Liang, Gan; Zhou, Ying-Xian; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">283</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon and aluminum oxide co-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode material has been successfully prepd. via a wet chem. method.  The effects of the hybrid layer coating of C and Al2O3 on cryst. structure, morphol. and electrochem. performance have been investigated.  It is found that C and Al2O3 co-coating can stabilize the structure and improve the cond. of NVPF.  As a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, the co-coated NVPF electrode shows a significant enhancement in rate capability and cycling performance, i.e., compared with bare NVPF, C-coated NVPF and Al2O3-coated NVPF, the NVPF/C-Al electrode delivers the highest capacity of 122.8 mAh g-1 with a superior capacity retention ratio of 95.6% after 100 cycles at 1 C.  This enhancement in cycling performance and rate capability can be ascribed to the protective effect of this hybrid coating layer of C and Al2O3 on NVPF from electrolyte attack and the facilitated electron/ion transmission caused by the hybrid coating layer.  This modification method of co-coating with electronic conductor C and sodium ionic cond. Al2O3 provides an effective way to improve the electrochem. properties of NVPF and other cathode materials with low electron/ion cond. for sodium/lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSMWRfV3kUjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsD0RiU86LOQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlKht73J&amp;md5=0354305552e85f3f84569339c0c8dd70</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c23793"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Performance Fe-Based Prussian Blue Cathode Material for Enhancing the Activity of Low-Spin Fe by Cu Doping</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Fe-Based Prussian Blue Cathode Material for Enhancing the Activity of Low-Spin Fe by Cu Doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Zhao-Yao; Fu, Xin-Yuan; Zhang, Lu-Lu; Yan, Bo; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron-based Prussian blue (FeHCF) has great application potential in the large-scale prodn. of sodium-ion (Na+) batteries because of its high theor. capacity and abundant Fe ore resources.  However, the Fe(CN)6 vacancies and crystal water seriously affect the electrochem. performance.  Herein, a Cu-doped FeHCF (Cu-FeHCF) cathode material is successfully prepd. directly by a copptn. method.  After Cu doping, the monoclinic structure and the quasi-cubic morphol. are retained, but the electrochem. performance is significantly improved.  In addn. to few Fe(CN)6 vacancies and low crystal water, the improved performance is also related to the enhanced electrochem. activity of low-spin Fe and the stabilizing effect of Cu on the crystal structure.  Moreover, Cu doping also controls the side reaction to a certain extent.  As a result, after Cu doping, the initial discharge capacity is enhanced from 107.9 to 127.4 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, esp. the capacities contributed by low-spin Fe increase from 30.0, 21.7, and 16.7 mA h g-1 to 48.8, 45.4, and 43.7 mA h g-1 for the first three cycles, resp.  Even at 2 A g-1, Cu-FeHCF still has a promising initial capacity of 82.3 mA h g-1 and only a 0.047% capacity decay rate for each cycle over 500 cycles.  Therefore, Cu-FeHCF shows excellent application potential in the field of Na+ energy storage batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGprOaiVam1wDrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsD0RiU86LOQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural regulated nickel hexacyanoferrate with superior sodium storage performance by K-doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei, Cheng; Fu, Xin-Yuan; Zhang, Lu-Lu; Liu, Jing; Sun, Pan-Pan; Gao, Lin; Chang, Kai-Jun; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue analogs with unique open frame structure have aroused great concern because of their low cost, environmental friendliness and relatively easy synthesis.  Esp., nickel hexacyanoferrate (NiHCF) attracts great attention due to its outstanding cycling stability.  Herein, we regulate the structure of NiHCF by K-doping at Na-site and investigate the sodium storage performance by combining expts. with d. functional theory calcns.  Our results reveal that K-doping induces the transformation of NiHCF from cubic to monoclinic and provides more sodium storage sites.  In addn., K+ ions can play a role of pillar in stabling the structure.  More importantly, K-doping can improve the transport ability of sodium ions and electrons.  As a result, the K-doped NiHCF electrode delivers an extremely high initial discharge capacity of 87.1 mAh g-1 at 10 mA g-1 with a very low capacity fading ratio of 0.016% per cycle at 800 mA g-1 over 1000 cycles.  Such K-doped NiHCF composite shows its potential application prospects in the field of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-aihdq-KsQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsD0RiU86LOQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisVWjurfN&amp;md5=1fccbc348c8a92ff1df6161f79a86090</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201802517"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.-B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Organic Carbonyl Compounds for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Recent Progress and Future Perspectives</span>. <i>Chem.─Eur.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Organic Carbonyl Compounds for Sodium-Ion Batteries: Recent Progress and Future Perspectives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Heng-guo; Zhang, Xin-bo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Na-org. batteries, which use org. materials as the electrodes in Na-ion batteries, are an attractive alternative to conventional Li-ion batteries for next-generation sustainable and versatile energy storage devices owing to the abundant Na resources and environmental friendly features.  However, orgs. used in Na-ion batteries also encounter some issues such as low redox potential, high soly. in the electrolyte, and low cond.  In response, altering the arom. system/attaching electron-withdrawing groups, constructing polymers, and incorporating a conductive matrix are effective strategies.  This review summarizes and briefly discusses recent org. carbonyl compds. for Na-org. batteries from the viewpoint of function-oriented design, including function evolution from small-mol. compds. to polymers, then composites, and finally flexible electrodes.  In particular, as a timely overview, carbonyl-based org. flexible electrodes for Na-org. batteries are also highlighted for the 1st time.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoPzFwofQho5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgsD0RiU86LOQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXit1OqtLjF&amp;md5=741f1c8f5584e73ac845a8b1e87d425d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.scriptamat.2020.02.023"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Microwave-Assisted Synthesis of Porous Nano-Sized Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@C Nanospheres for Sodium Ion Batteries with Enhanced Stability</span>. <i>Scripta Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>181</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">92</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">96</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">PTFE-derived carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode material for high-performance sodium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Chang; Zhang, Lu-Lu; Deng, Ze-Rong; Yan, Bo; Gao, Lin; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">432</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">141187</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) is considered to be a promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its large theor. capacity and high av. operating voltage.  However, the capacity is limited by its low intrinsic electronic cond. and the inevitable fluorine loss during synthesis.  Herein, carbon-coated NVPF composites were successfully synthesized using polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) as a carbon source and fluorine supplement agent.  The NVP impurity in these carbon-coated NVPF composites was significantly reduced or eliminated.  As a cathode material for SIBs, the optimized PTFE-derived carbon-coated NVPF exhibits excellent reversible capacity, superior rate capability, and considerable long-term cycle stability.  This simple and feasible modification strategy of using PTFE as a carbon source and fluorine supplement agent can also be extended to Na2FePO4F, LiVPO4F, K3V2(PO4)2F3, and other fluorine-contg. polyanionic cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZBmcna89uxLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFjBsWZq3JEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVyiur7L&amp;md5=e9e2d34afaf67d8342b7a99def0d074a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2018.12.131"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goh, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sui, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.-B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile One-Step Carbothermal Reduction Synthesis of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>/C Serving as Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile one-step carbothermal reduction synthesis of Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C serving as cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Deng, Liang; Sun, Gang; Goh, Kokswee; Zheng, Li-Li; Yu, Fu-Da; Sui, Xu-Lei; Zhao, Lei; Wang, Zhen-Bo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">298</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">459-467</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is considered to be a prospective candidate cathode for Na-ion batteries owing to its high operating voltage and excellent structural stability.  However, the cycle performance together with rate capability of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 was restrained on account of its low electronic cond.  C-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 samples were fabricated by using a facile 1-step carbothermal redn. method.  The well crystd. Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C showed good capacity performance where it delivered an initial discharge capacity of 112.3 mA h g-1 at 1C rate with a high retention of 89.7% after 100 cycles.  Even at the current rate of 8C, it could give a capacity of 64 mA h g-1.  The cycle stability of Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C at the high temp. of 55° was also demonstrated.  Besides, the Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C showed good long-term durability, of which the capacity loss averaged 0.0264% per cycle at 2C rate at room temp.  Also, the electrochem. impedance spectroscopy well explained the difference about the electrochem. performance of different Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C samples.  More importantly, Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C is of great competence to serve as cathode for future Na ion batteries applied in energy storage systems, and this simple 1-step carbothermal redn. strategy to get Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C will make contributions to accelerating this process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtLF7UDsrYR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFjBsWZq3JEw"> &gt;&gt; Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>516</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">230515</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2021.230515</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D516%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D230515%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DT.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BTang%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26author%3DD.%2BJia%26author%3DY.%2BGuo%26author%3DZ.%2BZhou%26title%3DIn%2BSitu%2BRedox%2BReaction%2BInduced%2BFirmly%2BAnchoring%2Bof%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%2Bon%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2B%2526%2BCarbon%2BNanosheets%2Bas%2BCathodes%2Bfor%2BHigh%2BStable%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2021.230515&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06830&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2021.230515&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ redox reaction induced firmly anchoring of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 on reduced graphene oxide &amp; carbon nanosheets as cathodes for high stable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yue; Wang, Ting; Tang, Yakun; Huang, Yudai; Jia, Dianzeng; Guo, Yong; Zhou, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">516</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">230515</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is considered as one of the most promising cathodes for sodium-ion batteries due to its high operating potential, fast ion transport and superior structural stability.  However, its poor rate capability and insufficient cyclability hinder its future practical applications.  Herein, a hybrid of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles firmly anchoring on reduced graphene oxide &amp; carbon (rGO&amp;C) nanosheets is synthesized through an in situ redox reaction.  The ethylenediamine and oxalic acid not only could induce the nucleation of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 along the surface of rGO, but also act as carbon sources of amorphous carbon, serving as binders to firmly and densely couple Na3V2(PO4)2F3 with the three-dimensional continuous conductive network constructed by rGO nanosheets.  The composite displays excellent rate capability and remarkable cycling stability (capacity retention of 81.9% for 1000 cycles at 30 C), due to the 2D rGO&amp;C nanosheets and anchored ultrafine Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles shorten diffusion length of the ions and electrons, the firm connectivity between Na3V2(PO4)2F3 and rGO&amp;C nanosheets enables high structure stability to relieve the stress and strain generated during the cycling.  The strategy can be extended to prep. other NASICON vanadium phosphates cathodes materials for advanced batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZ9qCcLWeHL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFjBsWZq3JEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitlamur3M&amp;md5=8e55bf504919fb550200a0d26962b34a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202310699"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Yolk-Shell Construction of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> with Copper Substitution Microsphere as High-Rate and Long-Cycling Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2310699</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering Crystal Growth and Surface Modification of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Cathode for High-Energy-Density Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Kang; Zhao, Hongshun; Li, Jianbin; Huang, Xiaobing; Jia, Shuyong; Chen, Wenkai; Ren, Yurong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) is a suitable cathode for sodium-ion batteries owing to its stable structure.  However, the large radius of Na+ restricts diffusion kinetics during charging and discharging.  Thus, in this study, a phosphomolybdic acid (PMA)-assisted hydrothermal method is proposed.  In the hydrothermal process, the NVPF morphologies vary from bulk to cuboid with varying PMA contents.  The optimal channel for accelerated Na+ transmission is obtained by cuboid NVPF.  With nitrogen-doping of carbon, the cond. of NVPF is further enhanced.  Combined with crystal growth engineering and surface modification, the optimal nitrogen-doped carbon-covered NVPF cuboid (c-NVPF@NC) exhibits a high initial discharge capacity of 121 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C.  Coupled with a com. hard carbon (CHC) anode, the c-NVPF@NC||CHC full battery delivers 118 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C, thereby achieving a high energy d. of 450 Wh kg-1.  Therefore, this work provides a novel strategy for boosting electrochem. performance by crystal growth engineering and surface modification.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-EuC-uZP5ULVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNMZdLfMsow"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase-pure Na3V2(PO4)2F3 embedded in carbon matrix through a facile polyol synthesis as a potential cathode for high performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Sohyun; Song, Jinju; Kim, Seyeon; Sambandam, Balaji; Mathew, Vinod; Kim, Sungjin; Jo, Jeonggeun; Kim, Seokhun; Kim, Jaekook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Research</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, a pseudo-layered Na super-ionic conductor of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF)/C cathode for sodium-ion batteries is prepd. successfully using a facile polyol refluxing process without any impurity phases.  The X-ray diffraction and Rietveld refinement results confirm that NVPF possesses tetragonal NASICON-type lattice with a space group of P42/mnm.  In this preparative method, polyol is utilized as a solvent as well as a carbon source.  The presence of nanosized NVPF particles in the carbon network is confirmed by field-emission SEM (FE-SEM) and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HR-TEM).  The existence of carbon is analyzed by Raman scattering and elemental anal. In addn., Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C composite achieved a retention capacity of ∼ 88% even after 1,500 cycles at 15 C.  Moreover, at high current densities of 30 and 50 C, Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C cathode retains the specific discharge capacities of 108.4 and 105.9 mAh·g-1, resp., revealing the structural stability of the material prepd. through a facile polyol refluxing method.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comprehensive review on the fabrication, modification and applications of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Lin; Wang, Hong; Sun, Dan; Tang, Yougen; Wang, Haiyan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Na-ion batteries (SIBs) have garnered tremendous interest due to their unique advantages of high safety, abundant Na resources, and low cost.  Great research efforts of SIBs have been devoted to the exploitation and in-depth mechanism investigation of high-performance electrode materials.  Among the various cathodes, Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF), a representative member of Na superionic conductor (NASICON) structured compds., has been considered to be a promising candidate because of its superior structural stability, fast ion transport, high operating potential and so on.  However, its electrochem. performance and future large-scale applications have been hindered by the relatively low electronic cond. and high cost of NVPF.  This review emphasizes the crystal structure and Na storage mechanisms together with synthetic methods of NVPF, and then summarizes various proposed strategies including carbon coating, element doping, size and morphol. design, etc. to meliorate the electrochem. performance of NVPF.  Addnl., the applications of the NVPF cathode in other battery systems are included.  Finally, our perspectives on the subsequent research and optimization of NVPF are also shared.  This review not only is a comprehensive summary of NVPF for the first time but also provides a good ref. for the rational design of high-performance NVPF in the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqzQmqlJ58j3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNMZdLfMsow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFegtLzK&amp;md5=a0d62a122cefca30bd6281263c15c0a6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/er.5397"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, W.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, C.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, G.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, S.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultra-Long Cycle Life and High Rate Performance Subglobose Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@C Cathode and Its Regulation</span>. <i>Int.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra-long cycle life and high rate performance subglobose sodium vanadium fluorophosphate and carbon cathode and its regulation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhan, Wen-xing; Fan, Chang-ling; Zhang, Wei-hua; Yi, Guo-dong; Chen, Han; Han, Shao-chang; Liu, Jin-shui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Energy Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A nitrogen-doped carbon coated subglobose Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C (NVPF) cathode for sodium-ion batteries was synthesized by using hexadecyl tri-Me ammonium bromide (CTAB) as soft template and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) as carbon source.  CTAB plays a significant role on the formation of sphere micelles.  Precursor ions are self-assembled on the surface at appropriate concn. and its mechanism is investigated in subglobose NVPF@C-4.  CTAB also increases the cond. of carbon layer as (CH3)3N+ in CTAB is combined with residual carbon from PVDF to form partially N-doped carbon.  Meanwhile, the carbon source PVDF contributes to prevent the generation of impurity Na3V2(PO4)3 by compensating the evaporative fluorine.  Generally, CTAB and PVDF play multifunctional roles in regulating Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C cathode with well-developed crystallite, high rate performance, good cond., and ultra-long cycle life.  The specific capacity of NVPF@C-4 cathode at 0.1 C and 10 C is as high as 121.5 mAh·g-1 and 99.2 mAh·g-1 with high capacity retention of 90.1% even after 1000 cycles at 10 C.  The excellent rate performance is also attributed to the high diffusion coeff. of Na+ and high exchange current according to the kinetic anal.  The enhanced electrochem. performances reveal the special regulation in this paper is feasible to obtain excellent structural stability of NVPF materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq5r7CjbRLLh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNMZdLfMsow"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtFKjsLzI&amp;md5=3407a4311192a988171e3174474041cb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE02641A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, K.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">With great superiorities in energy d., rate capability and structural stability, Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has attracted much attentions as cathode of sodium ion battery (SIB), but it also faces challenges on its poor intrinsic electronic cond. and the controversial de/sodiation mechanism.  Herein, a series of Zr-doped NVPF coated by N-doped carbon layer (∼5 nm in thickness, homogenously) materials are fabricated by a sol-gel method, and the optimized heteroatom-doping amts. of Zr and N doping improve intrinsic properties on enlarging lattice distance and enhancing electronic cond., resp.  Specifically, among all samples of Na3V2-xZrx(PO4)2F3/NC (NVPF-Zr-x/NC, x = 0, 0.01, 0.02, 0.05, and 0.1), the optimized electrode of NVPF-Zr-0.02/NC delivers high reversible capacities (119.2 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C), superior rate capability (98.1 mA h g-1 at 20 C) and excellent cycling performance.  The structural evolution of NVPF-Zr-0.02/NC electrode, in-situ monitored by X-ray diffractometer, follows a step-wise Na-extn./intercalation mechanism with reversible multi-phase changes, not just a solid-soln.-reaction one.  Full cells of NVPF-Zr-0.02/NC//hard carbon demonstrate high capacity (99.8 mA h g-1 at 0.5 C), high out-put voltage (3.5 V) and good cycling stability.  This work is favorable to accelerate the development of high-performance cathode materials and explore possible redox reaction mechanisms of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPvE6dn0DmSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljoNMZdLfMsow"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stabilizing fluorine to achieve high-voltage and ultra-stable Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Deng, Liang; Yu, Fu-Da; Xia, Yang; Jiang, Yun-Shan; Sui, Xu-Lei; Zhao, Lei; Meng, Xiang-Hui; Que, Lan-Fang; Wang, Zhen-Bo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">82</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">105659</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is a promising cathode candidate for sodium ion batteries due to its high working voltage.  However, an "unknown" low-voltage plateau around ∼3.3 V lowers its operating voltage and puzzles researchers.  Herein, the reasons for its appearance are explored.  It is found that the formation of the low-voltage plateau originates from the extra-generated [VO6] induced by the fluorine loss during the synthesis.  To enable better performance, a feasible strategy of stabilizing fluorine is proposed to eliminate the low-voltage plateau.  It is demonstrated that this strategy can effectively guarantee the existence of fluorine and modulate the local electronic structure of V to maintain [VO4F2] in Na3V2(PO4)2F3 phase, thus eliminating the undesirable plateau and achieving an operating-voltage increase of ∼100 mV.  Moreover, the enhanced structural stability and kinetics of the optimized Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode are confirmed by in-situ XRD.  As expected, the Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode delivers higher energy d. (446.4 Wh kg-1), better rate capability and longer cycling performance (89.2%@30 C after 1000 cycles).  Furthermore, its excellent adaptability to wide temp. range (-25 °C-55 °C) and strong competence in Na3V2(PO4)2F3||hard carbon full-cell are verified.  These excellent properties further qualifyNa3V2(PO4)2F3 as a competitive cathode for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqotNQB93Fpc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbzTk8R14jaw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXis12iur7L&amp;md5=00531c3e940b0ec463451006f17b6a1b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.0c00283"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N-Doped Carbon Nanotubes Decorated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> as a Durable Ultrahigh-Rate Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N-Doped Carbon Nanotubes Decorated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 as a Durable Ultrahigh-rate Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Taosheng; Zhang, Wei; Li, Huangxu; Hu, Junxian; Lai, Yanqing; Zhang, Zhian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3845-3853</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) is emerging as one of the most prospective cathodes for sodium ion batteries due to its robust structure, rapid diffusion of sodium ions, and high energy d.  However, the poor electronic cond. leads to unsatisfactory rate capability and insufficient cyclability.  Herein, the meticulous design and prepn. of NVPF particles anchored on N-doped carbon nanotubes is realized via a plain sol-gel method.  It demonstrates that a N-doped carbon nanotubes matrix can evidently boost the electronic/ionic cond. of the material and promote the charge transfer between the electrode and electrolyte interface.  Moreover, the patulous surface decorated with CNTs leads to the significant contribution of pseudocapacitance effect.  Consequently, the electrochem. characteristics of this NVPF particles in a N-doped electron-rich matrix are significantly enhanced, exhibiting a capacity of 126 mA h g-1 at 0.5 C and ultrahigh-rate capability of 76 mA h g-1 at 100 C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To overcome intrinsic low electronic conductance, delicately designed fiber-shape Na3V2(PO4)2F3@N-doped carbon composites (NVPF@C) have been prepd. for boosting Na-storage performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na superionic conductor structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has received considerable attention as a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries because of its higher energy d. and three-dimensional open structure for Na+ diffusion channels.  However, its insulating structure [PO4] results in significantly inferior cond., which severely limits the electrochem. performance of NVPF.  In this study, uniform carbonized polyacrylonitrile-coated hierarchical Na3V2(PO4)2F3 multi-clustered hollow microspheres (NVPF-H@cPAN) were synthesized via a facile ethylene glycol-assisted hydrothermal approach, followed by a wet chem. method and heat treatment. The concn. of ethylene glycol and hydrothermal reaction time were found to play essential roles in the formation mechanism of the microspheres.  The as-prepd. NVPF-H@cPAN delivered a high discharge capacity of 116.2 mAh g-1 at 0.2C and impressive cycling stability of 85% at 5C after 2000 cycles.  When assembled as NVPF-H@cPAN||com. hard carbon (NVPF-H@cPAN||CHC) for sodium-ion full cells, which demonstrates a specific capacity of 107 mAh g-1 at 0.2C, thus achieving an energy d. of 376.4 Wh kg-1 at a power d. of 141 W kg-1.  These results can be attributed to the structural regulation of multi-level clusters, which improved the Na+ diffusion rate and carbon coating strategy.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafast Potassium Storage in F-Induced Ultra-High Edge-Defective Carbon Nanosheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Yu; Yang, Yang; Xu, Rui; Cheng, Xiaolong; Huang, Huijuan; Shi, Pengcheng; Yao, Yu; Yang, Hai; Li, Dongjun; Zhou, Xuefeng; Chen, Qianwang; Feng, Yuezhan; Rui, Xianhong; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10217-10227</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials have been considered as promising anodes for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) because of their high electronic cond., eco-friendliness, and structural stability.  However, the small interlayer spacing and serious vol. expansion caused by the repeated insertion/extn. of large K-ions restrict their potassium-ion storage performance.  Herein, F and N codoped carbon nanosheets (FNCS) with rich-edge defects are designed to resolve these problems.  The F doping is in favor of the formation of more edge defects in the carbon layer, offering strong K+ adsorption capability and promoting the K+ storage.  The ultrathin carbon nanosheets can provide a large contact area for the electrochem. reactions and shorten the transportation pathways for both K-ions and electrons.  Consequently, the FNCS anode shows a high reversible capacity (610 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1) and ultrastable cyclability over 4000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Moreover, K-ion full cells (FNCS|K2FeFe(CN)6) display excellent cycling stability (128 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 500 cycles) and rate capability (93 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1).  This design strategy can be extended to design other electrode materials for high-performance energy storage, such as magnesium-ion batteries, supercapacitors, and electrocatalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoAKFmnqMKtebVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limCt0TDOwpAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtFCksr7F&amp;md5=e8b7f793779bd9894a310fa274bea763</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201500413"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Long, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-Dimensional Fluorinated Graphene: Synthesis, Structures, Properties and Applications</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Fluorinated Graphene: Synthesis, Structures, Properties and Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng Wei; Long Peng; Feng Yiyu; Li Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1500413</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Fluorinated graphene, an up-rising member of the graphene family, combines a two-dimensional layer-structure, a wide bandgap, and high stability and attracts significant attention because of its unique nanostructure and carbon-fluorine bonds.  Here, we give an extensive review of recent progress on synthetic methods and C-F bonding; additionally, we present the optical, electrical and electronic properties of fluorinated graphene and its electrochemical/biological applications.  Fluorinated graphene exhibits various types of C-F bonds (covalent, semi-ionic, and ionic bonds), tunable F/C ratios, and different configurations controlled by synthetic methods including direct fluorination and exfoliation methods.  The relationship between the types/amounts of C-F bonds and specific properties, such as opened bandgap, high thermal and chemical stability, dispersibility, semiconducting/insulating nature, magnetic, self-lubricating and mechanical properties and thermal conductivity, is discussed comprehensively.  By optimizing the C-F bonding character and F/C ratios, fluorinated graphene can be utilized for energy conversion and storage devices, bioapplications, electrochemical sensors and amphiphobicity.  Based on current progress, we propose potential problems of fluorinated graphene as well as the future challenge on the synthetic methods and C-F bonding character.  This review will provide guidance for controlling C-F bonds, developing fluorine-related effects and promoting the application of fluorinated graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRzjm9tNyCDMJ6KlWarZTAzfW6udTcc2eYZd3y0YP0fwbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1c%252FltFSruw%253D%253D&amp;md5=8551ff0e51f7d18f8cd52ae57ba65efb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.08.063"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hasa, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Buchholz, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effects of Nitrogen Doping on the Structure and Performance of Carbon Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>124</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">334</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">341</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of nitrogen doping on the structure and performance of carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 cathodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Huang; Hasa, Ivana; Buchholz, Daniel; Qin, Bingsheng; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">124</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) is a promising cathode material for sodium ion batteries due to the good electrochem. performance in terms of cycling stability and rate capability.  However, in order to access this performance a carbon coating is required to enhance the intrinsically poor material's cond.  Herein, we systematically investigate the role of N-doped carbon (NC) coatings on both the structural and electrochem. properties of NVP materials.  NC-coated NVP materials with various nitrogen contents have been rationally synthesized by a novel solid-state method allowing the selective N-doping of the carbon coating.  In fact, the N-doping changes the disorder and graphitic character of the carbon layer, strongly impacting the electrochem. performance of the NVP/C composite materials.  Results suggest that the appropriate N-doping amt. of the carbon leads to highly decreased electrode polarization and excellent cycling stability at high rate, enabling the NVP materials with high energy and power efficiencies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqG7eOhqysY5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limCt0TDOwpAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVyitL7I&amp;md5=c6e027b5daf5be1db8df0dce848bafed</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b10299"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, X.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polydopamine-Derived Nitrogen-Doped Carbon-Covered Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Cathode Material for High-Performance Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polydopamine-Derived Nitrogen-Doped Carbon-Covered Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Cathode Material for High-Performance Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Ma, Di; Li, Tao; Liu, Jing; Ding, Xiao-Kai; Huang, Yun-Hui; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
