The high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, high-angle annular dark-field images, and energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy analyses reveal that the NVPF/C-PDPA particles are covered by a complete and uniform covering layer, which is effective at preventing corrosion of NVPF in the electrolyte to greatly increase cycling stability.  Furthermore, N-doping into the carbon layer can produce addnl. active sites to improve the capacity esp. the rate capacity.  Such a NVPF/C-PDPA electrode delivers a remarkable rate capacity (98.0 mA h g-1 at 10 C) and superior cycle performance (∼95.8% capacity retention at 10 C after 800 cycles).                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design of two dimensional single crystalline Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanosheets for boosting Na+ migration and mitigating grain pulverization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xin; Wu, Qiao; Guo, Peng; Liu, Xiaojie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">439</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have received considerable attention as stationary energy storage applications.  However, it is still a challenge to develop high energy d. and stable cathode materials for SIBs.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3, as one of the most promising polyanion-type cathodes, has been explored due to its high reversible capacity and high discharge voltage.  In spite of excellent intrinsic features, poor rate capability ascribed to the intrinsically low electronic cond. and unsatisfactory ion cond., as well as grain pulverization, severely hinders their practical applications.  Based on d. functional theory calcns. and common knowledge about two dimensional materials, it is believed that rational design of two dimensional single cryst. Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanosheets could be an effective route to enhance Na+ migration and mitigate grain pulverization for high-performance SIBs.  Besides, combing Na3V2(PO4)2F3 and three-dimensional porous carbon, a composite of two dimensional Na3V2(PO4)2F3 wrapped with three dimensional porous carbon, was synthesized and utilized as cathode for SIBs.  When evaluated as cathode, NVPF@3Dc exhibits a high specific capacity of 131.5 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C, excellent rate property of 65.7 mAh g-1 at 10 C, and long lifespan of 2500 cycles with the capacity of 51.6 mAh g-1 at 5 C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGsCUSGMxpEbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0limCt0TDOwpAg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XntVWgurg%253D&amp;md5=25fbb7936489855fd5326f50b18d7c54</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/celc.202001514"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Graphene Network Decorated with Highly Symmetrical Cuboid Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Particles: High Rate Capability and Cycling Stability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">866</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">872</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-Dimensional Graphene Network Decorated with Highly Symmetrical Cuboid Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Particles: High Rate Capability and Cycling Stability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Shuyuan; Li, Huijun; Wang, Xiaomin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has captured significant heed for cathode materials of sodium-ion battery (SIB), owing to its stable three-dimensional (3D) structure channel that can accommodate Na+ diffusion.  However, NVPF is still facing with a major challenge in terms of the electrochem. performance, owing to its uncontrollable morphol.  Hence, it was fabricated by using a two-step hydrothermal method, whereby NVPF cuboid particles of homogenous morphol. and highly structural symmetry could anchor on the three-dimensional graphene network (GN) structure to form NVPF@GN.  The affiliation between the morphol. and performance of the NVPF@GN was further probed by manipulating the morphol. of the NVPF under diverse heat treatment temps.  When the temp. reaches 480 °C, NVPF@GN manifests prolonged cyclability (the capacity fading rate of 0.01 % cycle-1 at 0.5 C during 300 cycles) and it shows outstanding rate performance (when the rate is reset to 0.5 C, the capacity is 107 mAh g-1 and capacity retention is 99 %), which can be ascribed to the high structural symmetry of NVPF@GN.  These results indicate that NVPF@GN cuboids can be used as a prospective cathode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoTwJs2TxjZQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgGzZzfQTaKIw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXjvVeks78%253D&amp;md5=80c43a74758d40a1ebc5ed0542754d56</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2018.07.114"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cost-Effective Synthesis and Superior Electrochemical Performance of Sodium Vanadium Fluorophosphate Nanoparticles Encapsulated in Conductive Graphene Network as High-Voltage Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cost-effective synthesis and superior electrochemical performance of sodium vanadium fluorophosphate nanoparticles encapsulated in conductive graphene network as high-voltage cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Kelu; Lei, Ping; Wan, Xin; Zheng, Wenting; Xiang, Xingde</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">532</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">426-432</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium vanadium fluorophosphate (Na3(VO)2(PO4)2F, denoted as NVPF) has attracted particular interests as cathode for high-energy sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to the high working potential, high specific capacity, and robust structural framework.  However, it is challenged by the low electron cond. and lack of available facile synthesis method.  Herein, an environmentally benign, cost-effective synthesis route is reported to produce NVPF nanoparticles encapsulated in conductive graphene network (NVPF/C), involving low-temp. synthesis of NVPF nanoparticles in abs. aq. solvents and subsequent construction of conductive network through thermally induced transformation of graphene-oxide nanosheets. Exptl. results show that the optimized NVPF/C product possesses a three-dimensional graphene-encapsulation nanostructure composed of ∼100 nm NVPF nanoparticles and ∼4 nm carbon-coating layer.  The unique hierarchical structure enables it cycling with excellent electrochem. performance in terms of a high reversible capacity (116.4 mA h g-1 at 0.2 C), excellent high-rate capability (87.4 mA h g-1 at 10 C) and long-term lifetime (82.1% capacity retention after 1200 cycles).                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced electrochemical properties of W-doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C as cathode material in sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nongkynrih, Jeffry; Sengupta, Abhinanda; Modak, Brindaban; Mitra, Sagar; Tyagi, A. K.; Dutta, Dimple P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">415</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium super ion conductors (NASICON) based structures are being explored as cathode materials for application in sodium ion battery technol.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3 has been established as an important candidate in this category but suffers from low electronic cond.  In this work, the effect of the substitution of Tungsten (W) in place of Vanadium on the electrochem. performance of Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C in sodium ion battery (SIB) has been elucidated in detail.  The crucial role played by the synthesis method and the product morphol. on the electrochem. property of the cathode material has been highlighted.  The Na3V1.96W0.04(PO4)2F3@C cathode synthesized using sonochem. assisted sol gel followed by ball milling method exhibits improved structural integrity and enhanced Na-ion mobility.  The cathode delivers a high reversible capacity of 153 mAh g-1 at 0.1C.  Theor. studies indicate that incorporation of W reduces the band gap and improves the interfacial resistance of Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoqbtpSUSrCfLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgGzZzfQTaKIw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XosVams7s%253D&amp;md5=069c86c41da3f3e96f555841a5906c5d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.01.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Banks, C. E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Exploration of Ion Migration Mechanism and Diffusion Capability for Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Cathode Utilized in Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.01.025</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D256%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D258-263%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DW.%2BSong%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26author%3DZ.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DZ.%2BZhou%26author%3DF.%2BLi%26author%3DQ.%2BChen%26author%3DC.%2BE.%2BBanks%26title%3DExploration%2Bof%2BIon%2BMigration%2BMechanism%2Band%2BDiffusion%2BCapability%2Bfor%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%2BCathode%2BUtilized%2Bin%2BRechargeable%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2014.01.025&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06830&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2014.01.025&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exploration of ion migration mechanism and diffusion capability for Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode utilized in rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Weixin; Ji, Xiaobo; Wu, Zhengping; Yang, Yingchang; Zhou, Zhou; Li, Fangqian; Chen, Qiyuan; Banks, Craig E.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">256</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">258-263</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is employed as a promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries in order to explore the ion-migration mechanism and diffusion capability.  Two kinds of Na sites, namely Na(1) site and Na(2) site exist in the crystal structure per formula unit to accommodate a total of three sodium ions.  The ion at Na(2) site with half occupation exts. first and inserts the last due to its high chem. potential, while the whole extn./insertion of two ions between 1.6 and 4.6 V vs.  Na+/Na can produce three plateaus in charge/discharge processes because of the reorganization of ions.  The first discharge capacity of 111.6 mAh g-1 with retention of 97.6% after 50 cycles could be obtained by electrochem. testing at 0.091C.  Electrochem. activation and/or structural reorganization of the system by cycling could improve the diffusion coeff. of sodium with a comparatively large magnitude of 10-12 cm2 s-1, though many influences on the resistance factors also can be attributed to the cycling process.  Such work is of fundamental importance to the progression of sodium-based batteries to be fully realized and be implemented over existing Li-ion based batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsVPiAwYy6XLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgGzZzfQTaKIw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXjtFSktr0%253D&amp;md5=2c8e5d0a73263ec471d04d7552018830</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.133739"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, H.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of Zn-Substitution Induced Structural Regulation on Sodium Storage Performance of Fe-Based Prussian Blue</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>433</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">133739</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2021.133739</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D433%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D133739%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DL.-L.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.-Y.%2BChen%26author%3DX.-Y.%2BFu%26author%3DB.%2BYan%26author%3DH.-C.%2BTao%26author%3DX.-L.%2BYang%26title%3DEffect%2Bof%2BZn-Substitution%2BInduced%2BStructural%2BRegulation%2Bon%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BFe-Based%2BPrussian%2BBlue%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2021.133739&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06830&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2021.133739&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of zinc-substitution induced structural regulation on sodium storage performance of iron-based prussian blue</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Chen, Zhao-Yao; Fu, Xin-Yuan; Yan, Bo; Tao, Hua-Chao; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">433</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">133739</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe-based Prussian blue (Fe-PB) has attracted wide attention as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries due to its open frame structure, abundant iron ore resources, and simple prepn.  Nevertheless, the poor cycle performance caused by the [Fe(CN)6] defects and crystal water hinders its practical application.  Herein, the Fe-PB structure is regulated by Zn-substitution, and the effect of Zn-substitution induced structural regulation on sodium storage performance of Fe-PB is systematically investigated.  The d. functional theory calcn. results confirm that Zn-substitution can reduce the bandgap and decrease the energy barrier of Na+ ions migration.  Our expt. results further confirm the Zn-substituted Fe-PB composite (FeZn-PB) has a typical monoclinic structure with higher Na content, fewer [Fe(CN)6] vacancies and lower crystal water.  Moreover, Zn-substitution accelerates electrons and sodium ions migration and enhances the activity of both low-spin Fe and high-spin Fe.  As a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, the FeZn-PB electrode has a higher capacity and better cycle stability than Fe-PB.  Esp., FeZn-PB delivers an initial capacity as high as 145.0 mAh g-1 with a capacity contribution of 60.5 mAh g-1 from low-spin Fe at 20 mA g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1, FeZn-PB still delivers a high initial capacity of 98.5 mAh g-1 with a very low capacity decay rate per cycle of only 0.05% over 500 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqusmNaONplB7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljxZHDJs5r6Bw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXis1OjurfM&amp;md5=3d5730b7fc2f4b5ac21b75daecf61ff9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1002/cey2.142"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, P.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ternary Ni-Based Prussian Blue Analogue with Superior Sodium Storage Performance Induced by Synergistic Effect of Co and Fe</span>. <i>Carbon Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">827</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">839</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/cey2.142</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D827-839%26journal%3DCarbon%2BEnergy%26author%3DL.-L.%2BZhang%26author%3DC.%2BWei%26author%3DX.-Y.%2BFu%26author%3DZ.-Y.%2BChen%26author%3DB.%2BYan%26author%3DP.-P.%2BSun%26author%3DK.-J.%2BChang%26author%3DX.-L.%2BYang%26title%3DTernary%2BNi-Based%2BPrussian%2BBlue%2BAnalogue%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BPerformance%2BInduced%2Bby%2BSynergistic%2BEffect%2Bof%2BCo%2Band%2BFe%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fcey2.142&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06830&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fcey2.142&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ternary Ni-based Prussian blue analogue with superior sodium storage performance induced by synergistic effect of Co and Fe</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Wei, Cheng; Fu, Xin-Yuan; Chen, Zhao-Yao; Yan, Bo; Sun, Pan-Pan; Chang, Kai-Jun; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">827-839</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEANFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2637-9368</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Australia, Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue analog Na2Ni[Fe(CN)6] (Ni-PB) has been widely studied as a cathode material for sodium-ion battery due to its excellent cycling performance.  However, Ni-PB has a low theor. capacity of 85 mAh g-1 because of the electrochem. inertness of Ni.  Herein, ternary Ni-PB is successfully synthesized by double doping with Co and Fe at Ni-site, and the effect of doping with Co and Fe on the electrochem. performance of Ni-PB is systematically investigated through theor. calcns. and electrochem. tests.  The first principles calcns. confirm that double doping with Co and Fe can significantly reduce the energy barrier and bandgap of Ni-PB.  X-ray diffraction and compn. anal. results indicate that ternary NiCoFe-PB composite not only has good crystallinity and high Na content but also has low defects and crystal water.  Electrochem. tests reveal that, besides the capacity contribution of high-spin Co/Fe and low-spin Fe, Co-doping enhances the electrochem. activity of low-spin Fe and Fe-doping improves the activity of high-spin Co; moreover, double doping can decrease the diffusion resistance of Na+ ions through solid electrolyte interface film, accelerate the kinetics for both ion diffusion process and Faradic reaction, and increase active sites.  Under the synergistic effect of Co and Fe, this ternary NiCoFe-PB exhibits outstanding electrochem. performance with a high initial discharge capacity of 120.4 mAh g-1 at 20 mA g-1 and an extremely low capacity fading rate of 0.0044% per cycle at a high c.d. of 2 A g-1 even after 10,000 cycles, showing great application potential of ternary NiCoFe-PB in the field of large-scale energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9Fsn0eDM5KLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljxZHDJs5r6Bw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvVaksbjJ&amp;md5=610df823affb45e42e4b326c8cc1b952</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8b0faa65b325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47'],'ref48':['cit48'],'ref49':['cit49'],'ref50':['cit50']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0272-8842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the intrinsic electronic cond. of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF), zirconium (Zr) was introduced into the NVPF/C compd. through a carbothermal redn. reaction with citric acid as the carbon source.  The effects of Zr4+ doping on the crystal structure and morphol. of the as-prepd. materials were analyzed.  Electrochem. and kinetic properties of the samples were investigated by galvanostatic charge-discharge, CV and EIS test.  It is confirmed that moderate Zr4+ doping can improve the electrochem. performance of NVPF.  Among all Na3V2-xZrx(PO4)2F3/C (x = 0, 0.01, 0.05, 0.1) samples, Na3V1·95Zr0·05(PO4)2F3/C shows the best rate and cycle performance.  It exhibits the highest specific capacity of 121.8 and 110.3 mAh/g at 0.2 and 10 C, resp., and maintains a capacity retention of approx. 83.6% after 1000 cycles at 5 C.  The kinetic properties results show that the excellent electrochem. performance of Na3V1·95Zr0·05(PO4)2F3/C can be attributed to the increase in electronic cond. and ion diffusion coeff.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGocuKGVZkqh1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOjQtr9yFD5A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsF2itbjF&amp;md5=808628143b860ee11f9794c4ffee157e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.3c12772"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Puspitasari, D.                 10.1021/acsami.9b20490</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">N/P-Dual-Doped Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)2O2F Microspheres as a High-Performance Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Liu, Jing; Wei, Cheng; Sun, Pan-Pan; Gao, Lin; Ding, Xiao-Kai; Liang, Gan; Yang, Xue-Lin; Huang, Yun-Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3670-3680</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2O2F (NVPOF) is attracting great interest due to its large capacity and high working voltage.  However, poor electronic cond. limits the electrochem. performance of NVPOF.  Herein, we fabricate N/P-dual-doped carbon-coated NVPOF microspheres (labeled as NVPOF@P/N/C) via a hydrothermal process followed by heat treatment.  This microsphere-structured NVPOF@P/N/C composite has a relatively high tap d. of 1.22 g/cm3.  TEM and XPS results reveal that the dual-doped carbon layer is tightly coated on the NVPOF surface due to the bridging effect of P and has a good protective effect on NVPOF.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. confirm that a N/P-dual-doped carbon layer is advantageous to achieve higher electronic cond. and lower migration activation energy than those of the undoped and single N- or P-doped carbon layer.  As a cathode material for a sodium-ion battery (SIB), NVPOF@P/N/C exhibits high capacity (128 mAh/g at 0.5 C and 122 mAh/g at 2 C) and ultralong cycle performance (only 0.037% capacity fading rate per cycle in 500 cycles at 2 C).  We believe that the NVPOF@P/N/C composite is appealing for high-performance SIBs with large energy d.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoV3ugCQ6EW17Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoj2-aIXBy7g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXisVKktb%252FL&amp;md5=4d63803cf4d5a30b27fcdf44b786310f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1039/C8DT00062J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multi-Heteroatom Doped Carbon Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Derived from Ionic Liquids</span>. <i>Dalton Trans.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>47</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4259</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4266</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8DT00062J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multi-heteroatom doped carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 derived from ionic liquids</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Zhou, Ying-Xian; Li, Tao; Ma, Di; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">47</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4259-4266</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">DTARAF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1477-9226</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multi-heteroatom (N, S and F) doped carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 (labeled as NVP/C-ILs) derived from an ionic liq. 1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium bis(trifluoromethylsulfonyl)imide ([EMIM]TF2N) has been successfully fabricated.  The as-prepd. Na3V2(PO4)3 particles are well dispersed and closely coated with a multi-heteroatom (N, S and F) doped carbon layer.  As a cathode for sodium-ion batteries, the NVP/C-ILs electrode exhibits high reversible specific capacity (117.5 mA h g-1 at 1C), superior rate performance (93.4 mA h g-1 at 10C) and excellent cycling stability (∼95% capacity retention ratio at 10C over 1000 cycles).  The impressive electrochem. performance of NVP/C-ILs can be attributed to effectively conductive networks for electrons and Na+ ions induced by a joint effect of N, S and F doping on carbon.  The use of multi-heteroatom doped carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)3 provides a facile and effective strategy for the fabrication of high performance electrode materials with low intrinsic elec. cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqO6HYzDTDauLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoj2-aIXBy7g"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon and aluminum oxide co-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode material has been successfully prepd. via a wet chem. method.  The effects of the hybrid layer coating of C and Al2O3 on cryst. structure, morphol. and electrochem. performance have been investigated.  It is found that C and Al2O3 co-coating can stabilize the structure and improve the cond. of NVPF.  As a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, the co-coated NVPF electrode shows a significant enhancement in rate capability and cycling performance, i.e., compared with bare NVPF, C-coated NVPF and Al2O3-coated NVPF, the NVPF/C-Al electrode delivers the highest capacity of 122.8 mAh g-1 with a superior capacity retention ratio of 95.6% after 100 cycles at 1 C.  This enhancement in cycling performance and rate capability can be ascribed to the protective effect of this hybrid coating layer of C and Al2O3 on NVPF from electrolyte attack and the facilitated electron/ion transmission caused by the hybrid coating layer.  This modification method of co-coating with electronic conductor C and sodium ionic cond. Al2O3 provides an effective way to improve the electrochem. properties of NVPF and other cathode materials with low electron/ion cond. for sodium/lithium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSMWRfV3kUjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoj2-aIXBy7g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlKht73J&amp;md5=0354305552e85f3f84569339c0c8dd70</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c23793"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Performance Fe-Based Prussian Blue Cathode Material for Enhancing the Activity of Low-Spin Fe by Cu Doping</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron-based Prussian blue (FeHCF) has great application potential in the large-scale prodn. of sodium-ion (Na+) batteries because of its high theor. capacity and abundant Fe ore resources.  However, the Fe(CN)6 vacancies and crystal water seriously affect the electrochem. performance.  Herein, a Cu-doped FeHCF (Cu-FeHCF) cathode material is successfully prepd. directly by a copptn. method.  After Cu doping, the monoclinic structure and the quasi-cubic morphol. are retained, but the electrochem. performance is significantly improved.  In addn. to few Fe(CN)6 vacancies and low crystal water, the improved performance is also related to the enhanced electrochem. activity of low-spin Fe and the stabilizing effect of Cu on the crystal structure. As a result, after Cu doping, the initial discharge capacity is enhanced from 107.9 to 127.4 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, esp. the capacities contributed by low-spin Fe increase from 30.0, 21.7, and 16.7 mA h g-1 to 48.8, 45.4, and 43.7 mA h g-1 for the first three cycles, resp.  Even at 2 A g-1, Cu-FeHCF still has a promising initial capacity of 82.3 mA h g-1 and only a 0.047% capacity decay rate for each cycle over 500 cycles.  Therefore, Cu-FeHCF shows excellent application potential in the field of Na+ energy storage batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGprOaiVam1wDrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgoj2-aIXBy7g"> &gt;&gt; Herein, we regulate the structure of NiHCF by K-doping at Na-site and investigate the sodium storage performance by combining expts. with d. functional theory calcns.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Na-org. batteries, which use org. materials as the electrodes in Na-ion batteries, are an attractive alternative to conventional Li-ion batteries for next-generation sustainable and versatile energy storage devices owing to the abundant Na resources and environmental friendly features.  However, orgs. used in Na-ion batteries also encounter some issues such as low redox potential, high soly. in the electrolyte, and low cond.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) is considered to be a promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its large theor. capacity and high av. operating voltage.  However, the capacity is limited by its low intrinsic electronic cond. and the inevitable fluorine loss during synthesis.  Herein, carbon-coated NVPF composites were successfully synthesized using polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) as a carbon source and fluorine supplement agent.  The NVP impurity in these carbon-coated NVPF composites was significantly reduced or eliminated.  As a cathode material for SIBs, the optimized PTFE-derived carbon-coated NVPF exhibits excellent reversible capacity, superior rate capability, and considerable long-term cycle stability.  This simple and feasible modification strategy of using PTFE as a carbon source and fluorine supplement agent can also be extended to Na2FePO4F, LiVPO4F, K3V2(PO4)2F3, and other fluorine-contg. polyanionic cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZBmcna89uxLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzb-rDBIY4uA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVyiur7L&amp;md5=e9e2d34afaf67d8342b7a99def0d074a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2018.12.131"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goh, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sui, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.-B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile One-Step Carbothermal Reduction Synthesis of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>/C Serving as Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is considered to be a prospective candidate cathode for Na-ion batteries owing to its high operating voltage and excellent structural stability.  However, the cycle performance together with rate capability of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 was restrained on account of its low electronic cond.  C-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 samples were fabricated by using a facile 1-step carbothermal redn. method.  The well crystd. Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C showed good capacity performance where it delivered an initial discharge capacity of 112.3 mA h g-1 at 1C rate with a high retention of 89.7% after 100 cycles.  Even at the current rate of 8C, it could give a capacity of 64 mA h g-1.  The cycle stability of Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C at the high temp. of 55° was also demonstrated.  Besides, the Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C showed good long-term durability, of which the capacity loss averaged 0.0264% per cycle at 2C rate at room temp.  Also, the electrochem. impedance spectroscopy well explained the difference about the electrochem. performance of different Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C samples.  More importantly, Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C is of great competence to serve as cathode for future Na ion batteries applied in energy storage systems, and this simple 1-step carbothermal redn. strategy to get Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C will make contributions to accelerating this process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqtLF7UDsrYR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzb-rDBIY4uA"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is considered as one of the most promising cathodes for sodium-ion batteries due to its high operating potential, fast ion transport and superior structural stability.  However, its poor rate capability and insufficient cyclability hinder its future practical applications.  Herein, a hybrid of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles firmly anchoring on reduced graphene oxide &amp; carbon (rGO&amp;C) nanosheets is synthesized through an in situ redox reaction.  The ethylenediamine and oxalic acid not only could induce the nucleation of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 along the surface of rGO, but also act as carbon sources of amorphous carbon, serving as binders to firmly and densely couple Na3V2(PO4)2F3 with the three-dimensional continuous conductive network constructed by rGO nanosheets.  The composite displays excellent rate capability and remarkable cycling stability (capacity retention of 81.9% for 1000 cycles at 30 C), due to the 2D rGO&amp;C nanosheets and anchored ultrafine Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles shorten diffusion length of the ions and electrons, the firm connectivity between Na3V2(PO4)2F3 and rGO&amp;C nanosheets enables high structure stability to relieve the stress and strain generated during the cycling.  The strategy can be extended to prep. other NASICON vanadium phosphates cathodes materials for advanced batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZ9qCcLWeHL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzb-rDBIY4uA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitlamur3M&amp;md5=8e55bf504919fb550200a0d26962b34a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202310699"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Yolk-Shell Construction of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> with Copper Substitution Microsphere as High-Rate and Long-Cycling Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2310699</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) is a suitable cathode for sodium-ion batteries owing to its stable structure.  However, the large radius of Na+ restricts diffusion kinetics during charging and discharging.  Thus, in this study, a phosphomolybdic acid (PMA)-assisted hydrothermal method is proposed.  In the hydrothermal process, the NVPF morphologies vary from bulk to cuboid with varying PMA contents.  The optimal channel for accelerated Na+ transmission is obtained by cuboid NVPF.  With nitrogen-doping of carbon, the cond. of NVPF is further enhanced.  Combined with crystal growth engineering and surface modification, the optimal nitrogen-doped carbon-covered NVPF cuboid (c-NVPF@NC) exhibits a high initial discharge capacity of 121 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C.  Coupled with a com. hard carbon (CHC) anode, the c-NVPF@NC||CHC full battery delivers 118 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C, thereby achieving a high energy d. of 450 Wh kg-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Na-ion batteries (SIBs) have garnered tremendous interest due to their unique advantages of high safety, abundant Na resources, and low cost.  Great research efforts of SIBs have been devoted to the exploitation and in-depth mechanism investigation of high-performance electrode materials.  Among the various cathodes, Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF), a representative member of Na superionic conductor (NASICON) structured compds., has been considered to be a promising candidate because of its superior structural stability, fast ion transport, high operating potential and so on. This review emphasizes the crystal structure and Na storage mechanisms together with synthetic methods of NVPF, and then summarizes various proposed strategies including carbon coating, element doping, size and morphol. design, etc. to meliorate the electrochem. performance of NVPF.  Addnl., the applications of the NVPF cathode in other battery systems are included.  Finally, our perspectives on the subsequent research and optimization of NVPF are also shared.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A nitrogen-doped carbon coated subglobose Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C (NVPF) cathode for sodium-ion batteries was synthesized by using hexadecyl tri-Me ammonium bromide (CTAB) as soft template and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) as carbon source.  CTAB plays a significant role on the formation of sphere micelles.  Precursor ions are self-assembled on the surface at appropriate concn. and its mechanism is investigated in subglobose NVPF@C-4.  CTAB also increases the cond. of carbon layer as (CH3)3N+ in CTAB is combined with residual carbon from PVDF to form partially N-doped carbon.  Meanwhile, the carbon source PVDF contributes to prevent the generation of impurity Na3V2(PO4)3 by compensating the evaporative fluorine.  Generally, CTAB and PVDF play multifunctional roles in regulating Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C cathode with well-developed crystallite, high rate performance, good cond., and ultra-long cycle life.  The specific capacity of NVPF@C-4 cathode at 0.1 C and 10 C is as high as 121.5 mAh·g-1 and 99.2 mAh·g-1 with high capacity retention of 90.1% even after 1000 cycles at 10 C.  The excellent rate performance is also attributed to the high diffusion coeff. of Na+ and high exchange current according to the kinetic anal.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is a promising cathode candidate for sodium ion batteries due to its high working voltage.  However, an "unknown" low-voltage plateau around ∼3.3 V lowers its operating voltage and puzzles researchers.  Herein, the reasons for its appearance are explored.  It is found that the formation of the low-voltage plateau originates from the extra-generated [VO6] induced by the fluorine loss during the synthesis.  To enable better performance, a feasible strategy of stabilizing fluorine is proposed to eliminate the low-voltage plateau.  It is demonstrated that this strategy can effectively guarantee the existence of fluorine and modulate the local electronic structure of V to maintain [VO4F2] in Na3V2(PO4)2F3 phase, thus eliminating the undesirable plateau and achieving an operating-voltage increase of ∼100 mV.  Moreover, the enhanced structural stability and kinetics of the optimized Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode are confirmed by in-situ XRD.  As expected, the Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode delivers higher energy d. (446.4 Wh kg-1), better rate capability and longer cycling performance (89.2%@30 C after 1000 cycles).  Furthermore, its excellent adaptability to wide temp. range (-25 °C-55 °C) and strong competence in Na3V2(PO4)2F3||hard carbon full-cell are verified.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na superionic conductor structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has received considerable attention as a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries because of its higher energy d. and three-dimensional open structure for Na+ diffusion channels.  However, its insulating structure [PO4] results in significantly inferior cond., which severely limits the electrochem. performance of NVPF.  In this study, uniform carbonized polyacrylonitrile-coated hierarchical Na3V2(PO4)2F3 multi-clustered hollow microspheres (NVPF-H@cPAN) were synthesized via a facile ethylene glycol-assisted hydrothermal approach, followed by a wet chem. method and heat treatment.  Further, the possible formation mechanism of hierarchical Na3V2(PO4)2F3 multi-clustered hollow microspheres was investigated.  The concn. of ethylene glycol and hydrothermal reaction time were found to play essential roles in the formation mechanism of the microspheres.  The as-prepd. NVPF-H@cPAN delivered a high discharge capacity of 116.2 mAh g-1 at 0.2C and impressive cycling stability of 85% at 5C after 2000 cycles.  When assembled as NVPF-H@cPAN||com. hard carbon (NVPF-H@cPAN||CHC) for sodium-ion full cells, which demonstrates a specific capacity of 107 mAh g-1 at 0.2C, thus achieving an energy d. of 376.4 Wh kg-1 at a power d. of 141 W kg-1.  These results can be attributed to the structural regulation of multi-level clusters, which improved the Na+ diffusion rate and carbon coating strategy.  Such a combination of structural regulation and carbon-coating strategy can provide a strategy to synthesize materials with multi-level clusters of hollow microspheres to increase the electronic cond. and enhance the electrochem. performance of energy-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqOAodaF-8oRLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSjytoECkjFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvFKksb%252FM&amp;md5=926fc0b3c60ff787c97a4421f1cd590e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2021.138370"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, G.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, C.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, S.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of High Performance N-Doped Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>/C Cathode Assisting by Plasma Enhanced Chemical Vapor Deposition for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials have been considered as promising anodes for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) because of their high electronic cond., eco-friendliness, and structural stability.  However, the small interlayer spacing and serious vol. expansion caused by the repeated insertion/extn. of large K-ions restrict their potassium-ion storage performance.  Herein, F and N codoped carbon nanosheets (FNCS) with rich-edge defects are designed to resolve these problems.  The F doping is in favor of the formation of more edge defects in the carbon layer, offering strong K+ adsorption capability and promoting the K+ storage.  The ultrathin carbon nanosheets can provide a large contact area for the electrochem. reactions and shorten the transportation pathways for both K-ions and electrons.  Consequently, the FNCS anode shows a high reversible capacity (610 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1) and ultrastable cyclability over 4000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  Moreover, K-ion full cells (FNCS|K2FeFe(CN)6) display excellent cycling stability (128 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 500 cycles) and rate capability (93 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1).  This design strategy can be extended to design other electrode materials for high-performance energy storage, such as magnesium-ion batteries, supercapacitors, and electrocatalysis.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoAKFmnqMKtebVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljmlEqnU1ji4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtFCksr7F&amp;md5=e8b7f793779bd9894a310fa274bea763</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201500413"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Long, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Two-Dimensional Fluorinated Graphene: Synthesis, Structures, Properties and Applications</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Two-Dimensional Fluorinated Graphene: Synthesis, Structures, Properties and Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng Wei; Long Peng; Feng Yiyu; Li Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Fluorinated graphene, an up-rising member of the graphene family, combines a two-dimensional layer-structure, a wide bandgap, and high stability and attracts significant attention because of its unique nanostructure and carbon-fluorine bonds.  Here, we give an extensive review of recent progress on synthetic methods and C-F bonding; additionally, we present the optical, electrical and electronic properties of fluorinated graphene and its electrochemical/biological applications.  Fluorinated graphene exhibits various types of C-F bonds (covalent, semi-ionic, and ionic bonds), tunable F/C ratios, and different configurations controlled by synthetic methods including direct fluorination and exfoliation methods.  The relationship between the types/amounts of C-F bonds and specific properties, such as opened bandgap, high thermal and chemical stability, dispersibility, semiconducting/insulating nature, magnetic, self-lubricating and mechanical properties and thermal conductivity, is discussed comprehensively.  By optimizing the C-F bonding character and F/C ratios, fluorinated graphene can be utilized for energy conversion and storage devices, bioapplications, electrochemical sensors and amphiphobicity.  Based on current progress, we propose potential problems of fluorinated graphene as well as the future challenge on the synthetic methods and C-F bonding character.  This review will provide guidance for controlling C-F bonds, developing fluorine-related effects and promoting the application of fluorinated graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRzjm9tNyCDMJ6KlWarZTAzfW6udTcc2eY94rTgL4HX2bntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1c%252FltFSruw%253D%253D&amp;md5=8551ff0e51f7d18f8cd52ae57ba65efb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.08.063"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hasa, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Buchholz, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effects of Nitrogen Doping on the Structure and Performance of Carbon Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>124</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">334</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">341</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) is a promising cathode material for sodium ion batteries due to the good electrochem. performance in terms of cycling stability and rate capability.  However, in order to access this performance a carbon coating is required to enhance the intrinsically poor material's cond.  Herein, we systematically investigate the role of N-doped carbon (NC) coatings on both the structural and electrochem. properties of NVP materials.  NC-coated NVP materials with various nitrogen contents have been rationally synthesized by a novel solid-state method allowing the selective N-doping of the carbon coating.  In fact, the N-doping changes the disorder and graphitic character of the carbon layer, strongly impacting the electrochem. performance of the NVP/C composite materials.  Results suggest that the appropriate N-doping amt. of the carbon leads to highly decreased electrode polarization and excellent cycling stability at high rate, enabling the NVP materials with high energy and power efficiencies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqG7eOhqysY5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljmlEqnU1ji4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVyitL7I&amp;md5=c6e027b5daf5be1db8df0dce848bafed</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b10299"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, X.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polydopamine-Derived Nitrogen-Doped Carbon-Covered Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Cathode Material for High-Performance Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have received considerable attention as stationary energy storage applications.  However, it is still a challenge to develop high energy d. and stable cathode materials for SIBs.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3, as one of the most promising polyanion-type cathodes, has been explored due to its high reversible capacity and high discharge voltage.  In spite of excellent intrinsic features, poor rate capability ascribed to the intrinsically low electronic cond. and unsatisfactory ion cond., as well as grain pulverization, severely hinders their practical applications.  Based on d. functional theory calcns. and common knowledge about two dimensional materials, it is believed that rational design of two dimensional single cryst. Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanosheets could be an effective route to enhance Na+ migration and mitigate grain pulverization for high-performance SIBs.  Besides, combing Na3V2(PO4)2F3 and three-dimensional porous carbon, a composite of two dimensional Na3V2(PO4)2F3 wrapped with three dimensional porous carbon, was synthesized and utilized as cathode for SIBs.  When evaluated as cathode, NVPF@3Dc exhibits a high specific capacity of 131.5 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C, excellent rate property of 65.7 mAh g-1 at 10 C, and long lifespan of 2500 cycles with the capacity of 51.6 mAh g-1 at 5 C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGsCUSGMxpEbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljmlEqnU1ji4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XntVWgurg%253D&amp;md5=25fbb7936489855fd5326f50b18d7c54</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1002/celc.202001514"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Graphene Network Decorated with Highly Symmetrical Cuboid Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Particles: High Rate Capability and Cycling Stability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">866</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">872</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has captured significant heed for cathode materials of sodium-ion battery (SIB), owing to its stable three-dimensional (3D) structure channel that can accommodate Na+ diffusion.  However, NVPF is still facing with a major challenge in terms of the electrochem. performance, owing to its uncontrollable morphol.  Hence, it was fabricated by using a two-step hydrothermal method, whereby NVPF cuboid particles of homogenous morphol. and highly structural symmetry could anchor on the three-dimensional graphene network (GN) structure to form NVPF@GN.  The affiliation between the morphol. and performance of the NVPF@GN was further probed by manipulating the morphol. of the NVPF under diverse heat treatment temps.  When the temp. reaches 480 °C, NVPF@GN manifests prolonged cyclability (the capacity fading rate of 0.01 % cycle-1 at 0.5 C during 300 cycles) and it shows outstanding rate performance (when the rate is reset to 0.5 C, the capacity is 107 mAh g-1 and capacity retention is 99 %), which can be ascribed to the high structural symmetry of NVPF@GN.  These results indicate that NVPF@GN cuboids can be used as a prospective cathode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoTwJs2TxjZQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljmlEqnU1ji4A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXjvVeks78%253D&amp;md5=80c43a74758d40a1ebc5ed0542754d56</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2018.07.114"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cost-Effective Synthesis and Superior Electrochemical Performance of Sodium Vanadium Fluorophosphate Nanoparticles Encapsulated in Conductive Graphene Network as High-Voltage Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium vanadium fluorophosphate (Na3(VO)2(PO4)2F, denoted as NVPF) has attracted particular interests as cathode for high-energy sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to the high working potential, high specific capacity, and robust structural framework.  However, it is challenged by the low electron cond. and lack of available facile synthesis method.  Herein, an environmentally benign, cost-effective synthesis route is reported to produce NVPF nanoparticles encapsulated in conductive graphene network (NVPF/C), involving low-temp. synthesis of NVPF nanoparticles in abs. aq. solvents and subsequent construction of conductive network through thermally induced transformation of graphene-oxide nanosheets.  The resultant product is structurally and electrochem. investigated by combining X-ray diffraction, fourier transform IR spectroscopy, scanning electron microscope, transition electron microscope, and electrochem. anal.  Exptl. results show that the optimized NVPF/C product possesses a three-dimensional graphene-encapsulation nanostructure composed of ∼100 nm NVPF nanoparticles and ∼4 nm carbon-coating layer.  The unique hierarchical structure enables it cycling with excellent electrochem. performance in terms of a high reversible capacity (116.4 mA h g-1 at 0.2 C), excellent high-rate capability (87.4 mA h g-1 at 10 C) and long-term lifetime (82.1% capacity retention after 1200 cycles).
