                        rightTab-cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exploration of ion migration mechanism and diffusion capability for Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode utilized in rechargeable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Weixin; Ji, Xiaobo; Wu, Zhengping; Yang, Yingchang; Zhou, Zhou; Li, Fangqian; Chen, Qiyuan; Banks, Craig E.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">256</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">258-263</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is employed as a promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries in order to explore the ion-migration mechanism and diffusion capability.  Two kinds of Na sites, namely Na(1) site and Na(2) site exist in the crystal structure per formula unit to accommodate a total of three sodium ions.  The ion at Na(2) site with half occupation exts. first and inserts the last due to its high chem. potential, while the whole extn./insertion of two ions between 1.6 and 4.6 V vs.  Na+/Na can produce three plateaus in charge/discharge processes because of the reorganization of ions.  The first discharge capacity of 111.6 mAh g-1 with retention of 97.6% after 50 cycles could be obtained by electrochem. testing at 0.091C.  Electrochem. activation and/or structural reorganization of the system by cycling could improve the diffusion coeff. of sodium with a comparatively large magnitude of 10-12 cm2 s-1, though many influences on the resistance factors also can be attributed to the cycling process.  Such work is of fundamental importance to the progression of sodium-based batteries to be fully realized and be implemented over existing Li-ion based batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpsVPiAwYy6XLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljCXox6Ny1RCQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXjtFSktr0%253D&amp;md5=2c8e5d0a73263ec471d04d7552018830</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.133739"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, H.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of Zn-Substitution Induced Structural Regulation on Sodium Storage Performance of Fe-Based Prussian Blue</span>. <i>Chem. Eng. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>433</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">133739</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cej.2021.133739</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of zinc-substitution induced structural regulation on sodium storage performance of iron-based prussian blue</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Chen, Zhao-Yao; Fu, Xin-Yuan; Yan, Bo; Tao, Hua-Chao; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">433</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">133739</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe-based Prussian blue (Fe-PB) has attracted wide attention as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries due to its open frame structure, abundant iron ore resources, and simple prepn.  Nevertheless, the poor cycle performance caused by the [Fe(CN)6] defects and crystal water hinders its practical application.  Herein, the Fe-PB structure is regulated by Zn-substitution, and the effect of Zn-substitution induced structural regulation on sodium storage performance of Fe-PB is systematically investigated.  The d. functional theory calcn. results confirm that Zn-substitution can reduce the bandgap and decrease the energy barrier of Na+ ions migration.  Our expt. results further confirm the Zn-substituted Fe-PB composite (FeZn-PB) has a typical monoclinic structure with higher Na content, fewer [Fe(CN)6] vacancies and lower crystal water.  Moreover, Zn-substitution accelerates electrons and sodium ions migration and enhances the activity of both low-spin Fe and high-spin Fe.  As a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, the FeZn-PB electrode has a higher capacity and better cycle stability than Fe-PB.  Esp., FeZn-PB delivers an initial capacity as high as 145.0 mAh g-1 with a capacity contribution of 60.5 mAh g-1 from low-spin Fe at 20 mA g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1, FeZn-PB still delivers a high initial capacity of 98.5 mAh g-1 with a very low capacity decay rate per cycle of only 0.05% over 500 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqusmNaONplB7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljCXox6Ny1RCQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXis1OjurfM&amp;md5=3d5730b7fc2f4b5ac21b75daecf61ff9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref50" class="rightTabRefNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit50" data-doi="10.1002/cey2.142"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, P.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ternary Ni-Based Prussian Blue Analogue with Superior Sodium Storage Performance Induced by Synergistic Effect of Co and Fe</span>. <i>Carbon Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">827</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">839</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/cey2.142</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ternary Ni-based Prussian blue analogue with superior sodium storage performance induced by synergistic effect of Co and Fe</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lu-Lu; Wei, Cheng; Fu, Xin-Yuan; Chen, Zhao-Yao; Yan, Bo; Sun, Pan-Pan; Chang, Kai-Jun; Yang, Xue-Lin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">827-839</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEANFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2637-9368</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons Australia, Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue analog Na2Ni[Fe(CN)6] (Ni-PB) has been widely studied as a cathode material for sodium-ion battery due to its excellent cycling performance.  However, Ni-PB has a low theor. capacity of 85 mAh g-1 because of the electrochem. inertness of Ni.  Herein, ternary Ni-PB is successfully synthesized by double doping with Co and Fe at Ni-site, and the effect of doping with Co and Fe on the electrochem. performance of Ni-PB is systematically investigated through theor. calcns. and electrochem. tests.  The first principles calcns. confirm that double doping with Co and Fe can significantly reduce the energy barrier and bandgap of Ni-PB.  X-ray diffraction and compn. anal. results indicate that ternary NiCoFe-PB composite not only has good crystallinity and high Na content but also has low defects and crystal water.  Electrochem. tests reveal that, besides the capacity contribution of high-spin Co/Fe and low-spin Fe, Co-doping enhances the electrochem. activity of low-spin Fe and Fe-doping improves the activity of high-spin Co; moreover, double doping can decrease the diffusion resistance of Na+ ions through solid electrolyte interface film, accelerate the kinetics for both ion diffusion process and Faradic reaction, and increase active sites.  Under the synergistic effect of Co and Fe, this ternary NiCoFe-PB exhibits outstanding electrochem. performance with a high initial discharge capacity of 120.4 mAh g-1 at 20 mA g-1 and an extremely low capacity fading rate of 0.0044% per cycle at a high c.d. of 2 A g-1 even after 10,000 cycles, showing great application potential of ternary NiCoFe-PB in the field of large-scale energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9Fsn0eDM5KLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljCXox6Ny1RCQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvVaksbjJ&amp;md5=610df823affb45e42e4b326c8cc1b952</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c06830</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Materials characterization, electrochemical tests, equations for calculating sodium ion diffusion coefficient using Warburg factor and GITT data, the electrochemical performance of PTFE-modified samples, cell parameters of NC@NVPF and NC/C@NVPF before and after cycling, average discharge capacity, the first charge/discharge curves of PTFE-modified samples, the first charge/discharge curves and cycle performance of DA-modified samples, NC@NVPF-N<sub>PTFE</sub>, and NC/C@NVPF, F 1s high-resolution XPS spectra, CV curves, and electrochemical performance of CHC anode (<a <script nonce="90da8b0faa65b325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
